Defense of the Exception Classification in Muhrim's Penalties
Author defends the consistency of his earlier exception claim by showing each penal case has a separate legal basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the six penalty cases presented by the author, classify them as either a disconnected exception (istithna' munqati') or an independent ruling, and explain the distinct legal cause for each.

Core Idea
Not every apparent exception is a true exception—each ruling has its own distinct cause.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a potential confusion: if he earlier claimed there is a single exception, how can there be multiple cases that look like exceptions? He dismantles each case systematically, showing that they are not exceptions to a general rule but independent rulings with their own legal causes. This is a masterclass in legal taxonomical precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's core claim
State the author's principal assertion: 'there is no exception at all.' Understand that this claim appears to contradict the earlier mention of a single exception, which the author resolves by clarifying that the earlier case is a 'disconnected exception' (istithna' munqati') — not a true exception.
The author is defending logical consistency, not changing his position.
2
Analyze each penalty case separately
Examine the cases: (1) the book's issue (istithna' munqati'), (2) ifadah (returning) – a missed wajib of Hajj, (3) tawaf in janabah – a missed wajib of tawaf, (4) killing game after wuquf – two dams per madhhab, (5) shaving before slaughter – nothing on mufrid, (6) cutting trees of Haram – a pure penalty unrelated to ihram. For each, note the specific cause (sabab) of the ruling.
Distinguish between violations of ihram (jinaayah 'ala al-ihram) and violations of specific obligations.
3
Understand the principle of independent causes
The author emphasizes that each ruling is tied to its own cause. For example, tawaf in janabah obligates a dam not because of ihram but because of leaving a wajib of tawaf. This is proven by the fact that a non-muhrim also owes a dam for the same action. Generalize: every wajib of Hajj is independent; 'Umrah has no connection with most of them.
This principle prevents the multiplication of penalties for a qarin unless the act specifically relates to both Hajj and 'Umrah.
4
Analyze the two cases involving the Haram
Distinguish between cutting trees of the Haram (a pure penalty, unrelated to ihram) and killing game of the Haram by a qarin (which involves two values due to the multiple ihram). The author uses the rule that the stronger of two sanctities subsumes the weaker; here ihram is stronger, so the obligation is solely due to ihram, not the Haram.
If the killer is non-muhrim, the penalty is due to the Haram alone (single value).
5
Synthesize the author's defense
Tie together: the author's earlier statement about a single exception referred to a specific disconnected exception; the other cases are not exceptions but independent rulings. The apparent contradiction vanishes when each case's cause is identified. Recognize this as a standard Hanafi technique of precision in legal causation.
The author's method reinforces the importance of asbab (causes) in deriving rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبطل بيع المستثنى عدة مسائل لا مسألة واحدة والتحقيق أنه لا استثناء أصلاً. أما مسألة الكتاب فقد قدمنا أنه استثناء منقطع، وأما مسألة الإفاضة فإنما وجب دم بسبب ترك واجب من واجبات الحج وليس هو جناية على الإحرام كما قدمناه ولا خصوصية لهذا الواجب بل كل واجب من واجبات الحج فإنه لا تعلق للعمرة به. وأما مسألة الطواف جنباً فإنما وجب دم واحد لترك واجب من واجبات الطواف لا للجناية على الإحرام، ولهذا لو طاف جنباً وهو غير محرم فإنه يلزمه دم وإن كان الدم متنوعاً إلى بدنة وشاة نظراً إلى كمال الجناية وخفتها. وأما مسألة قتل الصيد بعد الوقوف فالمذهب لزوم دمين وما في الأجناس ضعيف كما قدمناه. وأما مسألة الحلق قبل الذبح فإنه لا يلزم المفرد به شيء لأن الذبح ليس بواجب عليه، وهم إنما أوجبوا التعدد على القارن فيما يلزم المفرد به كفارة وليس على المفرد به شيء فلا يتعدد الدم على القارن. وأما مسألة قطع شجر الحرم فهو من باب الغرامات لا تعلق للإحرام به بخلاف صيد الحرم إذا قتله القارن فإنه يلزمه قيمتان كما صرح به الأسبيجاني وغيره لأنها جناية على الإحرام وهو متعدد كما قدمنا أن أقوى الحرمتين تستتبع أدناهما والإحرام أقوى فكان وجوب القيمة بسبب الإحرام فقط لا بسبب الحرم، وإنما ينظر إلى الحرم إذا كان القاتل حلالاً والله سبحانه الموفق.
And the sale of the exception is invalid [in] several issues, not one issue, and the reality is that there is no exception at all. As for the issue of the book, we have already stated that it is a disconnected exception. As for the issue of ifadah, a dam is obligated only due to leaving an obligatory act of Hajj, and it is not a crime against ihram as we have stated, and there is no specificity for this obligatory act; rather, every obligatory act of Hajj is such that 'Umrah has no connection with it. As for the issue of tawaf while in janabah, a single dam is obligated due to leaving an obligatory act of tawaf, not for a crime against ihram; for this reason, if one performs tawaf while in janabah and he is not a muhrim, a dam is still obligated upon him, although the dam varies between a badanah and a sheep according to the completeness and lightness of the crime. As for the issue of killing game after standing [at 'Arafah], the madhhab is that two dams are due, and what is in al-Ajnas is weak as we have stated. As for the issue of shaving before slaughter, nothing is obligated upon the mufrid because slaughter is not obligatory upon him; they only obligated multiplicity for the qarin in what obligates a kaffarah upon the mufrid, and nothing is upon the mufrid, so the dam does not multiply for the qarin. As for the issue of cutting trees of the Haram, it is from the chapter of penalties; ihram has no connection with it, unlike game of the Haram if the qarin kills it, for two values are obligated upon him as stated by al-Asbajani and others, because it is a crime against ihram, and it is multiple, as we have stated that the stronger of the two sanctities subsumes the weaker, and ihram is stronger; so the obligation of the value is due to ihram only, not due to the Haram, and consideration is given to the Haram only if the killer is a non-muhrim. And Allah Almighty is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
The author addresses a potential criticism: someone might think that his earlier statement about a single exception (istithna') contradicts the fact that several rules seem to be exceptions. He clarifies that each case is a separate ruling and not an exception to a general principle. The case in the book (the original matn case) is indeed a disconnected exception (istithna' munqati'). The case of ifadah (returning from Mina) requires a dam because an obligatory act of Hajj was missed, not because of ihram. Similarly, tawaf while in janabah incurs a dam for missing an obligatory act of tawaf, not for ihram; therefore a non-muhrim also owes dam for janabah tawaf. Killing game after standing at 'Arafah requires two dams according to the madhhab, not one. Shaving before slaughter imposes nothing on a mufrid (one performing Hajj only) because slaughter is not obligatory on him; thus a qarin does not owe multiple dams on that account. Cutting trees of the Haram is a pure penalty unrelated to ihram, unlike killing game of the Haram by a qarin, which involves ihram (hence two values). Thus the author defends the consistency of his rulings.

Key Terms
استثناء منقطع (istithna' munqati'): A disconnected exception; a ruling that appears to be an exception but is actually a separate category with its own cause.
دم (dam): A blood offering (sacrifice) required as a penalty for missing an obligatory act in Hajj or 'Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does a qarin who kills game in the Haram owe two dam (values) rather than one?
A) Because the Haram and ihram each create a separate obligation, requiring two dam.
B) Because the stronger sanctity (ihram) subsumes the weaker (Haram), so only one dam is considered.
C) Because it is a crime against ihram, and the qarin has multiple ihrams (Hajj and 'Umrah), thus two values.
D) Because killing game in the Haram always requires two dam, regardless of ihram.

Key Takeaway
The author's defense shows that legal taxonomy requires identifying the specific cause of each ruling; apparent exceptions may be independent categories with distinct asbab.

Joint Killing of Game: Penalties for Halal, Mufrid, and Qarin
Expanding the matn's ruling on joint game killing with detailed calculations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the penalty for each category of person (halal, mufrid, qarin) when jointly killing game in the Haram, applying the Hanafi rules of contribution and sequential injury.

Core Idea
Penalties for joint killing depend on ihram status and whether actions are simultaneous or sequential.

This lesson unpacks the detailed scenario of three different types of people—a non-muhrim (halal), a mufrid (Hajj-only), and a qarin (Hajj and 'Umrah)—jointly killing game in the Haram. The base ruling gives a quick fraction, but the author then expands on the underlying principles that determine each person's share. Understanding these calculations is crucial for correctly applying liability when multiple parties are involved in a single violation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their ihram status
Determine whether each killer is halal, mufrid, or qarin. This affects the baseline penalty: halal pays 1/3, mufrid 1, qarin 2.
The qarin owes double because of two ihrams.
2
Assess whether the killing was by a single joint action or separate sequential actions
If simultaneous and combined, the penalty is shared equally; if separate, each pays for their own damage plus the remaining joint part.
Simultaneous separate strikes require splitting the residual value.
3
Calculate the damage caused by each wound
If injuries are separate, compute the reduction in value caused by each wound.
A wound on a healthy animal reduces value more than on an already wounded one.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule of joint causation
When actions combine, the liable amount is split; when sequential, the later actor is liable only for the reduction from the already-wounded state.
The first actor is liable for damage to the healthy animal; subsequent actors for damage to the diminished value.
5
Combine the baseline and injury calculations
For each party, sum their individual liability from direct damage plus shared liability, then apply the ihram multiplier (1/3, 1, or 2) to get the final penalty.
The halal's multiplier reduces his share relative to muhrims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشترك حلال ومفرد وقارن في قتل صيد الحرم فعلى الحلال ثلث الجزاء، وعلى المفرد جزاء كامل، وعلى القارن جزاءان ا هـ . ولم يبين المصنف الجزاء الذي يجب على الحلالين بقتل صيد الحرم مع أن فيه تفصيلاً وهو أنهما إن ضرباه ضربة واحدة فمات كان على كل واحد منهما نصف قيمته صحيحاً، وإن ضربه كل واحد منهما ضربة فإن وقعا معاً فإنه يجب على كل واحد منهما ما نقصته جراحته، ثم يجب على كل واحد منهما نصف قيمته مجروحاً بجراحتين لأن عند اتحاد فعلهما جميع الصيد صار متلفاً بفعلهما فضمن كل نصف الجزاء، وعند الاختلاف الجزء الذي تلف بضربة كل هو المختص بإتلافه فعليه جزاؤه والباقي متلف بفعلهما فعليهما ضمانه. وإن كان الضارب له حلالاً ومحرماً كذلك ضمن كل واحد ما نقصته جراحته ثم يضمن الحلال نصف قيمته مضروباً بالضربتين وعلى المحرم قيمته مضروباً بالضربتين ولو لم يقعا معاً بأن جرحه الحلال أولاً ثم ثنى المحرم ضمن الحلال ما انتقص بجرحه صحيحاً ونصف قيمته وبه الجراحتان لأن النقصان حصل بالجرح وهو صحيح والهلاك حصل بأثر الفعل وهو منقوص بالجراحتين وعلى المحرم قيمته وبه الجرح الأول لأنه جرح كان منقوصاً بالجرح الأول. ولو قطع حلال يد صيد ثم فقأ محرم عينه ثم جرحه قارن فمات فعلى الحلال قيمته كاملة لأنه استهلكه معنى وهو صحيح لأنه فوت عليه جنس المنفعة، وعلى الثاني قيمته وبه الجرح الأول لأنه استهلكه معنى وعلى القارن قيمتان وبه الجنايات لأنه أتلفه حقيقة بأثر الفعل وهو منقوص بهما.
A non-muhrim, a mufrid, and a qarin jointly killed game of the Haram: upon the non-muhrim is one-third of the penalty, upon the mufrid is a complete penalty, and upon the qarin are two penalties. End. And the author did not clarify the penalty that is obligated upon two non-muhrims for killing game of the Haram, although there is detail: if they struck it with one blow and it died, upon each of them is half of its value in a healthy state; if each struck it once, and they occurred simultaneously, then upon each is what his wound diminished, then upon each is half of its value wounded by two wounds, because when their actions are united, the entire game became destroyed by their action, so each guarantees half of the penalty; when their actions differ, the part destroyed by each's blow is specifically his destruction, so he owes its penalty, and the remainder is destroyed by their joint action, so they both guarantee it. If the striker includes a non-muhrim and a muhrim, similarly each guarantees what his wound diminished, then the non-muhrim guarantees half of its value struck by the two strokes, and upon the muhrim is its value struck by the two strokes. If they did not occur simultaneously, such as the non-muhrim wounded it first, then the muhrim followed, the non-muhrim guarantees what was diminished by his wound on a healthy animal and half its value with both wounds, because the reduction occurred by the wound while it was healthy, and death occurred by the effect of the act while it was diminished by two wounds; and upon the muhrim is its value with the first wound, because the wound was diminished by the first wound. If a non-muhrim cut the hand of game, then a muhrim gouged out its eye, then a qarin wounded it and it died, then upon the non-muhrim is its full value because he caused its effective destruction while it was healthy, since he deprived it of the kind of benefit; upon the second is its value with the first wound because he caused effective destruction; and upon the qarin are two values with the injuries, because he caused actual destruction by the effect of the act while it was diminished by both.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage provides detailed scenarios for joint killing of game in the Haram by different categories: a halal (non-muhrim), a mufrid (one performing only Hajj), and a qarin (one performing Hajj and 'Umrah together). The base ruling from the matn is that the halal pays one-third of a single penalty, the mufrid pays one full penalty (since he is muhrim once), and the qarin pays two full penalties (since he is in two ihrams). The author then expands on cases where two non-muhrims jointly kill game: if they strike together, each pays half the value; if separately but simultaneously, each pays for his own wound plus half the remaining value; if sequentially, the first pays for the damage done to the healthy animal plus half the remaining value, and the second pays the full value minus the first's wound. Then he mixes a halal and a muhrim: similar calculations apply, but the muhrim pays more because of his ihram. Finally, an example with three different perpetrators (halal, muhrim, qarin) causing different injuries sequentially: the halal pays full value because he destroyed the game's function while healthy; the muhrim pays value minus the first wound; the qarin pays two values (for the two ihrams) with the injuries. The calculations are based on the principle that each perpetrator is liable for the damage he directly caused, and for the joint destruction they share equally.

Key Terms
مفرد (mufrid): A person performing Hajj only (ifrad), without 'Umrah; here contrasted with qarin.
قارن (qarin): A person performing Hajj and 'Umrah together in one ihram (qiran); owes double penalties for crimes against ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a halal, a mufrid, and a qarin jointly kill game of the Haram, what is the penalty for the qarin?
A) One full penalty
B) Two full penalties
C) One-third of a penalty
D) Half a penalty

Key Takeaway
The penalty for jointly killing game in the Haram is not a simple equal split; it depends on each killer's ihram status and the nature of their contribution.

Invalidity of Sale of Game by a Muhrim
Ruling with reasoning on muhrim's sale of game, with liability details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim's sale of game, distinguish between batil and fasid in this context, and apply the liability rules when the game perishes or is killed.

Core Idea
A muhrim cannot own live game, so selling it is batil; if caught while halal and sold while muhrim, the sale is fasid and both owe a penalty.

This lesson examines a specific fiqh ruling from the chapter of Hajj and Buyu': the invalidity of a muhrim (person in ihram) selling or purchasing game. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the reasoning behind the ruling and explores nuanced scenarios, including the liability of the buyer when the game perishes and the refinement by al-Ramli distinguishing between batil (void) and fasid (irregular). Understanding this ruling clarifies the limits of property ownership and contractual capacity during ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening statement: 'ويبطل بيع المحرم صيداً أو شراؤه'. Identify the act (sale/purchase of game) and the subject (muhrim). Determine the hukm: invalid (batil). Note that this applies to live game (صيد حي), not dead game which is carrion.
The word 'صيد' here refers to live game; dead game is obviously invalid to sell.
2
Understand the ta'lil (reasoning)
The passage cites the reasoning from al-Hidayah: selling live game is an exposure to loss of security (تعرض للصيد بفوات الأمن), and selling dead game is carrion. Recognize that this is a rational proof (qiyas) based on the inability of a muhrim to own game and the prohibition of harming it.
The reasoning shows that the invalidity is due to the lack of ownership and the violation of ihram.
3
Analyze the liability scenarios
The text presents two scenarios: (1) The seller caught the game while muhrim: if the game perishes in the buyer's hand, the buyer owes no compensation to the seller because the seller never owned it. (2) The seller caught the game while halal (non-muhrim) but later became muhrim and sold it: the buyer guarantees the value to the seller, and both owe a complete penalty (jaza') for the killing.
In scenario 2, the seller originally owned the game but lost the right to sell it upon entering ihram.
4
Examine al-Ramli's refinement
Al-Ramli notes that the sale in scenario 2 is fasid (irregular), not batil. The author's general statement that the sale is 'invalid' applies specifically when both parties are muhrim. When only the seller is muhrim, the sale is fasid, meaning it has some effect (e.g., the buyer must pay the value).
This refinement clarifies an apparent contradiction and shows the precision of later Hanafi commentators.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
Consider a modern scenario: a hunter catches a deer while not in ihram, then enters ihram for Hajj and sells the live deer to another muhrim. The sale is fasid; the buyer owes the value and both owe a penalty. If the deer dies in the buyer's hand, the buyer still owes the value because the seller owned it initially.
The ruling emphasizes that ihram restricts property transactions involving game.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويبطل بيع المحرم صيد أو شراؤه لأن بيعه حياً تعرض للصيد بفوات الأمن وبيعه بعد ما بيع ميتة. كذا علله في الهداية والظاهر من الصيد هو الحي، وأما الميتة فمعلوم بطلان بيعها. وأشار إلى أنه لو هلك في يد المشتري فإنه لا ضمان عليه للبائع إذا كان اصطاده البائع وهو محرم لأنه لم يملكه. وإن كان قد اصطاده وهو حلال ثم أحرم فباعه فإن المشتري يضمن له قيمته، وأما الجزاء فعلى كل واحد جزاء كامل لأن البائع جنى بالبيع والمشتري بالشراء حين قتله. قوله : (وإن كان قد اصطاده وهو حلال) الخ قال الرملي فيه دلالة على أن البيع في هذه الصورة فاسد، وبه صرح في النهر مع أنه داخل في عموم كلام المصنف، وكلامه صريح في المشتري محرم أيضاً فيكون مخرجاً لكلام المصنف عن الإطلاق، فقوله سواء كانا محرمين أو أحدهما الخ مستدرك فتأمله . وقوله وإن كان قد اصطاده وهو حلال» إلى قوله يضمن له قيمته وأما الجزاء فعلى كل واحد يصلح جواباً لما ألغز به بعضهم بقوله : عندي سؤال حسن مستظرف فرع على أصلين قد تفرعا أتلف شيئاً برضا مالكه ويضمن القيمة
His saying: (And the sale by a muhrim of game or its purchase is invalid), because selling it while alive is an exposure of the game to loss of security, and selling it after it has been sold [as dead] is [selling] a dead body. Thus it is reasoned in al-Hidayah, and the apparent meaning of 'game' is the live one, while the dead one is known to be invalid to sell. And he indicated that if it perishes in the hand of the buyer, there is no guarantee upon him towards the seller if the seller caught it while he was a muhrim, because he did not own it. If he had caught it while he was a non-muhrim (halal), then became a muhrim and sold it, then the buyer guarantees its value to him, and as for the penalty, upon each one is a complete penalty, because the seller committed a crime by selling and the buyer by purchasing when he killed it. His saying: (If he had caught it while he was halal...) al-Ramli said: there is indication that the sale in this scenario is fasid (irregular), and it is stated explicitly in al-Nahr, even though it falls under the generality of the author's words; and his words are explicit that the buyer is also a muhrim, thus it excludes the author's words from absoluteness. So his saying 'whether both are muhrim or one of them' is superfluous, so consider it. And his saying 'If he had caught it while halal...' up to his saying 'the buyer guarantees its value to him, and as for the penalty, upon each one' is suitable as an answer to what some have posed as a riddle: 'I have a good pleasant question, a branch that has branched from two principles: one destroys something with the owner's consent and guarantees the value.'
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that a muhrim cannot validly sell or buy game. The reasoning from al-Hidayah is that selling a live game is a form of exposing it to insecurity, and selling dead game is obviously invalid as it is carrion. The author then discusses liability: if the game perishes in the buyer's hand, the buyer owes nothing to the seller if the seller caught it while muhrim (since he never owned it). If the seller caught it while halal and later became muhrim and sold it, the buyer must pay the value to the seller, and both owe a complete penalty (jaza') because each committed a violation: the seller by selling (enabling the killing) and the buyer by purchasing and then killing the game. The author then quotes al-Ramli who refines the ruling: the sale is fasid (irregular) in this scenario, and the author's general statement that the sale is invalid applies specifically when both are muhrim; if only one is, the ruling differs. The final riddle is answered: if someone destroys something with the owner's consent, he still guarantees the value, applied here to the buyer.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Game animal that is hunted; here specifically referring to live game in the Haram.
فاسد (fasid): Irregular sale; one that has some deficiency but may have some effect, as opposed to batil (void).
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty for killing game while in ihram; here both seller and buyer owe a complete penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Ramli, what is the ruling when a muhrim sells a game that he caught while halal (non-muhrim)?
A) The sale is batil (void)
B) The sale is fasid (irregular)
C) The sale is valid but sinful
D) The sale is valid and permissible

Key Takeaway
A muhrim cannot validly sell or buy live game; the sale is batil if both are muhrim, and fasid if only the seller is muhrim, and both parties are liable for the penalty if the game is killed.

Invalidity of Sale of Game by a Muhrim
Ruling with proof and consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the sale of game by a muhrim is batil and derive it from Quran 5:96 using the concept of haram al-ayn.

Core Idea
Game is not property for a muhrim, so any sale or purchase is void ab initio.

This passage examines a unique intersection of Hajj and Buyu' jurisprudence: the transaction of game by a person in ihram. The commentator not only declares the sale void but also explains the underlying reasoning—the game is haram al-ayn (prohibited in itself) for the muhrim, similar to wine for a Muslim. This fundamental principle removes the item from being māl (valuable property), making any contract involving it completely void. Understanding this helps distinguish between batil (void) and fasid (irregular) transactions and clarifies the separate penalty (jaza') for the offense of trading game while in ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the sale or purchase of game (صيد) by a person in ihram. The ruling is that the transaction is batil (void), not fasid (irregular). This means it has no legal effect and does not transfer ownership.
Batil transactions cannot be ratified; they are null from the start.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The evidence is Quran 5:96: 'وَحُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمًا' (Forbidden to you is the game of the land as long as you are in ihram). Note that the prohibition is attached to the 'ayn (essence) of the game.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) but zanni al-dalala (probable meaning) because it requires interpretation.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Because Allah added the prohibition to the 'ayn (the substance), it indicates that game becomes haram al-ayn for the muhrim. This removes its status as māl (valuable property), just like wine for a Muslim. Since a valid sale requires the subject matter to be māl, the contract is void.
Contrast with fasid: in a fasid contract, the item is still property but the contract has a flaw. Here, the item is not property at all.
4
Apply the ruling to different scenarios
The ruling applies regardless of whether the other party is also muhrim or halal. If a halal seller sells to a muhrim buyer, the sale is batil. If both are muhrim, both incur a penalty (jaza'). The penalty is separate from the void contract.
The penalty is a religious liability, not a consequence of the contract.
5
Understand the practical consequence
If the game perishes with the buyer, the seller cannot claim compensation because the buyer never owned it. However, if the seller was halal when he hunted it and later became muhrim and sold it, the buyer (if halal) must pay the value to the seller as compensation for the game, but the contract is still batil.
This scenario shows a nuance: the value is not the price but a compensation for the destroyed property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويبطل بيع المحرم صيد أو شراؤه لأن بيعه حياً تعرض للصيد بفوات الأمن وبيعه بعد ما بيع ميتة. كذا علله في الهداية والظاهر من الصيد هو الحي، وأما الميتة فمعلوم بطلان بيعها. وأشار إلى أنه لو هلك في يد المشتري فإنه لا ضمان عليه للبائع إذا كان اصطاده البائع وهو محرم لأنه لم يملكه. وإن كان قد اصطاده وهو حلال ثم أحرم فباعه فإن المشتري يضمن له قيمته، وأما الجزاء فعلى كل واحد جزاء كامل لأن البائع جنى بالبيع والمشتري بالشراء. وإنما كان البيع باطلاً ولم يكن فاسداً لأن الصيد في حق المحرم محرم العين بقوله تعالى وحرم عليكم صيد البر ما دمتم حرما) [المائدة : ٩٦] أضاف التحريم إلى العين فأفاد سقوط التقوم في حقه كالخمر في حق المسلم. وحاصله إخراج العين عن المحلية لسائر التصرفات فيكون التصرف فيها عبثاً فيكون قبيحاً لعينه فيبطل، سواء كانا محرمين أو أحدهما، ولهذا أطلقه المصنف فإنه أفاد أن بيع المحرم باطل ولو كان المشتري حلالاً، وأن شراء باطل وإن كان البائع حلالاً. وأما الجزاء فإنما يكون على المحرم حتى لو كان البائع حلالاً والمشتري محرم لزم المشتري فقط، وعلى هذا كل تصرف فإن وهب صيداً فإن كانا محرمين لزم كل واحد جزاء، وإن كان أحدهما محرماً لزمه فقط ولو تبايعا صيداً في الحل ثم أحرما أو أحدهما ثم وجد المشتري به رجع بالنقصان وليس له الرد. وعلى هذا لو غصب حلال صيد حلال ثم أحرم الغاصب والصيد في يده لزمه إرساله وضمان قيمته للمغصوب منه، فلو لم يفعل ودفعه إلى المغصوب منه حتى برئ من الضمان له كان عليه الجزاء وقد أساء وهذا لغز؛ يقال غاصب يجب عليه عدم الرد بل إذا فعل يجب به الضمان فلو أحرم المغصوب منه ثم دفعه إليه فعلى كل واحد منهما الجزاء. لا هذا حلال باع صيداً محرماً فما حمى إحرامه وما رعى وأتلف الصيد المبيع جانباً مضمن القيمة والمثل معاً ا هـ . قلت : لكن فيه أن المبيع فاسداً يملكه المشتري بالقبض فالمالك هنا المشتري هو البائع قوله : (فلو لم يفعل ودفعه إلى المغصوب منه الخ) أقول : وجوب الجزاء في هذه الصورة مشكل عند قول المتن ولو أخذ حلال صيداً فأحرم ضمن مرسله من أنه قد أتلفه المرسل فيضمنه لما مر والواجب عليه ترك التعرض ويمكنه ذلك بأن يخليه في بيته فإذا قطع يده عنه كان متعدياً ا هـ.
His saying: (The sale of game by a muhrim is invalid, and so is its purchase, because selling it alive is an exposure of the game to loss of safety, and selling it after it has been sold is a dead [transaction]. Thus it is explained in al-Hidayah. The apparent meaning of 'game' is the live animal; as for the dead, its sale is known to be invalid. He indicated that if it perishes in the hand of the buyer, there is no liability on the seller if the seller hunted it while in ihram, because he did not own it. If he had hunted it while halal and then entered ihram and sold it, then the buyer guarantees its value to him, and as for the penalty, each owes a full penalty because the seller committed an offense by selling and the buyer by purchasing. It was a batil (void) sale, not fasid (irregular), because game, in relation to a muhrim, is haram al-ayn (prohibited in essence) by the saying of Allah: 'And forbidden to you is the game of the land as long as you are in ihram' (al-Ma'idah 96). He added prohibition to the essence, indicating the loss of monetary value in his regard, like wine in the regard of a Muslim. The upshot is that the essence is removed from being eligible for all dispositions, so disposing of it is futile and thus ugly in itself, so it is void, whether both are muhrim or one of them. For this reason the author (al-Kashghari) gave it as absolute, indicating that the sale by a muhrim is void even if the buyer is halal, and purchase is void even if the seller is halal. As for the penalty, it is only on the muhrim—if the seller is halal and the buyer is muhrim, it is only incumbent on the buyer. Similarly in every disposition: if one gives game as a gift and both are muhrim, each owes a penalty; if one is muhrim, only that one owes. If two people trade game in the hill (non-Haram area) and then both or one of them enters ihram, and then the buyer finds a defect, he may recover the decrease but cannot return it. Similarly, if a halal person usurps game from another halal, then the usurper enters ihram while the game is in his hand, he must release it and guarantee its value to the owner. If he does not do so and instead hands it over to the owner, thereby becoming free from guarantee, he still owes the penalty and acts wrongfully. This is a riddle: It is said that a usurper must not return [in this state], but if he does, it incurs liability. If the owner then enters ihram and hands it back, each owes a penalty. No! This is a halal person who sold game that is muhrim (in the sense of being protected)? He did not protect his ihram nor observe [the rules], and destroyed the game sold, guaranteeing both value and a like. End. I say: But in this, the sold item in a fasid sale is owned by the buyer upon possession, so the owner here is the buyer, not the seller. His saying: (If he does not do so and hands it over to the usurped owner, etc.) I say: The obligation of the penalty in this situation is problematic based on the matn's statement: 'If a halal takes game and then enters ihram, the one who sent it guarantees it', as he has destroyed it by sending it, so he guarantees it, as previously mentioned. The obligated person must avoid interference, and he can do so by leaving it in his house; if he removes his hand from it, he is transgressing. End.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the invalidity of sale and purchase of game (صيد) by a person in ihram (muhrim). The commentator explains that the transaction is batil (void) rather than fasid (irregular), because for a muhrim, game is considered haram al-ayn (prohibited in essence), similar to wine for a Muslim. The primary evidence is Quran 5:96, which prohibits hunting game while in ihram, indicating that the very substance is not property for a muhrim. Thus, any disposition (sale, purchase, gift) is void. The ruling applies regardless of whether the other party is also muhrim or halal. However, the penalty (جزاء) is only on the muhrim party involved. The commentary also covers a scenario where a halal person hunted the game before ihram and then sells it after entering ihram: the buyer must pay the value to the seller, but both incur a penalty because the sale is an offense. The passage then discusses a usurper (غاصب) who becomes muhrim while holding game: he must release it and pay its value to the owner. If he instead returns it, he still owes a penalty. This leads to a riddle about a ghasib who must not return the game but if he does, he incurs liability; further, if the owner then becomes muhrim and returns it, both owe a penalty. The commentator partially resolves the riddle but notes a difficulty in one scenario based on another matn statement. The overall theme is that game is legally valueless for the muhrim, so transactions are void and each muhrim party incurs a penalty.

Key Terms
محرم العين (haram al-ayn): Something prohibited in its very essence, such that it is not considered property for a Muslim (like wine) or for a muhrim (like game).
جزاء (jaza'): A penalty (usually sacrificial animal or monetary compensation) for violating ihram prohibitions.
باطل (batil): Void ab initio; a contract that does not transfer ownership and has no legal effect.
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, bound by specific prohibitions.

D) Because the buyer is always a muhrim

Key Takeaway
Sale or purchase of game by a muhrim is batil because game is haram al-ayn for him, and each muhrim party incurs a separate penalty for the offense.

Removing a Female Gazelle from the Haram: Compensation and Offspring
Ruling with juristic reasoning (talil) on compensation for Haram game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for offspring born after compensation is paid, and apply Ibn al-Humam's distinction between ability and inability to return the animal.

Core Idea
Paying compensation for a Haram animal ends its protected status only if return is impossible.

This lesson explores a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding game taken from the Haram (sanctuary). The matn states that if someone removes a female gazelle and she gives birth, he is liable for both if they die. However, if he pays compensation before the birth, he is not liable for the offspring. The commentary reveals that this hinges on whether the animal retains its protected status. Ibn al-Humam deepens the analysis by distinguishing between cases where the taker can still return the animal and where he cannot. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of Haram sanctity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling from the matn
Read the matn carefully. It gives two scenarios: (1) removing a pregnant gazelle that gives birth and both die → he guarantees both. (2) Paying compensation for the mother before birth → no liability for offspring. State these clearly.
The ruling is a clear rule: liability for offspring is tied to the timing of compensation payment.
2
Understand the legal attribute of protected status (hurma)
The commentary explains that the game, even after removal, remains 'muhtaram' (protected) by law. This legal attribute extends to the offspring because it attaches to the mother. This is why the offspring are also protected until compensation is paid.
The concept of 'protected status' is a key legal fiction in Hanafi fiqh for Haram animals.
3
Recognize the principle 'arrival of substitute is like arrival of original'
When compensation (khalaf) is paid, it substitutes the original animal. This principle ends the protected status of the mother because the substitute 'arrives' in place of the original. Thus, the mother loses her sanctity and, by extension, the offspring are not born into that sanctity.
This principle (وصول الخلف كوصول الأصل) is a legal maxim used here to justify the change in status.
4
Apply Ibn al-Humam's two-case analysis
The muhaqqiq (Ibn al-Humam) adds a critical condition: if the taker is able to return the animal to the Haram, paying compensation does NOT remove the prohibition; he must still return it. Only if he is unable (e.g., the animal escapes) does the compensation serve as expiation, freeing him from further liability and allowing him to even hunt the animal.
This distinction refines the matn and is the mufta bihi position in later Hanafi fatwa.
5
Distinguish the practical consequences
Based on the two cases, determine the ruling for a real scenario: (a) If someone has the gazelle in his possession after paying compensation, he must return it and cannot slaughter it. (b) If the gazelle escapes, he is free and may even hunt it if it leaves the Haram.
The practical difference is whether the prohibition (hurma) remains after compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن أخرج ظبية الحرم فولدت فاتا ضمنهما فإن أدى جزاءها فولدت لا يضمن الولد) لأن الصيد بعد الإخراج من الحرم بقي مستحق إلا من شرعاً ولهذا وجب رده إلى مأمنه، وهذه صفة شرعية فتسري إلى الولد فإن أدى جزاءها ثم ولدت ليس عليه جزاء الولد لأن بعد أداء الجزاء لم تبق آمنة لأن وصول الخلف كوصول الأصل، ولهذا يملكها الذي أخرجها بعد أداء الجزاء، ولهذا لو ذبحها لم تكن ميتة لكنه مكروه ـ كذا قالوا ـ وقد بحث فيه المحقق في فتح القدير فقال : والذي يقتضيه النظر أن أداء الجزاء إن كان حال القدرة على إعادة مأمنها بالرد إلى المأمن لا يقع كفارة ولا يحل بعده التعرض له بل حرمة التعرض إليها قائمة، وإن كان حال العجز عنه بأن هربت في الحل بعد ما أخرجها إليه خرج به عن عهدتها فلا يضمن ما يحدث بعد التكفير من أولادها وله أن يصطادها، وهذا لأن.
His saying: (Whoever takes out a female gazelle from the Haram and she gives birth, and both die, he guarantees both. If he pays her compensation and then she gives birth, he does not guarantee the offspring.) Because the game, after being taken out of the Haram, remains legally protected (muhtaram) as before, and therefore it must be returned to its place of safety. This is a legal attribute that extends to the offspring. If he pays the compensation for her and then she gives birth, he is not liable for the offspring because after paying the compensation, she is no longer in the state of being protected (amnah), for the arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original. Therefore, the one who took her out owns her after paying the compensation. For this reason, if he slaughtered her, she would not be carrion (mayta), but it is disliked (makruh) — so they said. The muhaqqiq (Ibn al-Humam) discussed this in Fath al-Qadir and said: The view that is necessitated by consideration is that the payment of compensation, if it is at a time when he is able to return her to her place of safety by returning her to the sanctuary, does not constitute expiation and after it, it is not permissible to interfere with her; rather, her prohibition remains in effect. If it is at a time of inability, e.g., she escaped into the open area after he had taken her out, he thereby becomes free of liability, so he is not liable for what occurs after the expiation of her offspring, and he may hunt her. This is because...
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with juristic reasoning (talil) about compensation for removing a female gazelle from the Haram (sanctuary of Mecca). The matn states that if someone takes out a gazelle and she gives birth, and both die, he guarantees both. If he pays the compensation (jaza') for the mother and then she gives birth, he does not guarantee the offspring. The commentator explains the reason: the game, after being removed, still retains its protected status (hurma) by law, so it must be returned to its safe place. This attribute extends to the offspring. But after paying compensation, the mother loses her protected status because the substitute (the compensation) takes the place of the original. Thus, the taker becomes the owner after payment, and slaughtering her would not make her carrion (though it is disliked). The commentator then cites the muhaqqiq (Ibn al-Humam) who differentiates between two cases: if the compensation is paid while the taker is able to return the gazelle to the sanctuary, it does not remove the prohibition, and he must still return her. If the gazelle has escaped and he cannot return her, then the compensation serves as expiation, he is free of liability, and he may even hunt her. This shows the nuanced Hanafi view on how compensation interacts with the protected status of Haram game.

Key Terms
ظبية (zabyah): A female gazelle or deer; a type of wild game that is protected in the Haram.
مأمن (ma'man): The safe place or sanctuary (i.e., the Haram) to which the animal must be returned.
خلف (khalaf): Substitute; the compensation paid takes the place of the original animal, affecting its legal status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Humam's refined view, when does paying compensation for a Haram animal lift the prohibition on interfering with it?
A) Always, because compensation substitutes the animal.
B) Only when the taker is unable to return the animal to the Haram.
C) Only if the animal gives birth after compensation.
D) Never; compensation never lifts the prohibition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on Haram game compensation is nuanced: paying compensation ends protected status only when return is impossible, a refinement crucial for correct fatwa.

Why a Muhrim's Sale of Game is Void (Batil)
Ruling with proof on invalidity of Muhrim's sale of game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a Muhrim's sale of game is batil, explain the Quranic proof and the concept of 'muharram al-'ayn', and apply the rule to related transactions like gifts and usurpation.

Core Idea
Game is essentially prohibited for a Muhrim, so it has no legal value and any transaction with it is void (batil).

The Hanafi school holds that a person in the state of ihram (Muhrim) cannot validly sell game because the game itself is prohibited for them. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this ruling, grounded in the Qur'anic verse that attaches prohibition to the essence of game, and examines the practical consequences for sales, gifts, and usurpation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
Note that the author states the sale of game by a Muhrim is batil (void), not fasid (voidable). Understand the difference: batil means the contract has no legal effect, while fasid is irregular but may be corrected.
In Hanafi fiqh, batil cannot become valid; fasid can be rectified by removing the defect.
2
Locate the proof from Quran
The proof is verse 5:96: 'Forbidden to you is game of the land as long as you are in ihram.' The key is that prohibition is attached to the 'ayn (essence) of the game, not merely to the act of hunting.
This differentiates it from a prohibition on use (like during fasting) which would render the sale fasid, not batil.
3
Understand the legal consequence: removal of taqawwum
Because the game is essentially prohibited for a Muhrim, it loses its property value (taqawwum) in their regard. A Muhrim cannot own game or derive benefit from it, so any transaction is futile (ʿabath) and thus intrinsically repugnant (qabīḥ li-ʿaynihi).
This is analogous to wine for a Muslim: it has no legal value.
4
Apply the principle to various scenarios
The passage extends the ruling: sale is batil whether both parties are Muhrim or only one; gift and other transactions follow the same rule; the penalty (jazaʾ) falls only on the Muhrim; if a halal person usurps game and then becomes Muhrim, he must release it and pay compensation.
These applications demonstrate the consistent application of the underlying principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً فولدت لا يضمن الولد والأخذ. وإنما كان البيع باطلاً ولم يكن فاسداً لأن الصيد في حق المحرم محرم العين بقوله تعالى وحرم عليكم صيد البر ما دمتم حرما) [المائدة : ٩٦] أضاف التحريم إلى العين فأفاد سقوط التقوم في حقه كالخمر في حق المسلم. وحاصله إخراج العين عن المحلية لسائر التصرفات فيكون التصرف فيها عبثاً فيكون قبيحاً لعينه فيبطل، سواء كانا محرمين أو أحدهما، ولهذا أطلقه المصنف فإنه أفاد أن بيع المحرم باطل ولو كان المشتري حلالاً، وأن شراء باطل وإن كان البائع حلالاً. وأما الجزاء فإنما يكون على المحرم حتى لو كان البائع حلالاً والمشتري محرم لزم المشتري فقط، وعلى هذا كل تصرف فإن وهب صيداً فإن كانا محرمين لزم كل واحد جزاء، وإن كان أحدهما محرماً لزمه فقط ولو تبايعا صيداً في الحل ثم أحرما أو أحدهما ثم وجد المشتري به رجع بالنقصان وليس له الرد. وعلى هذا لو غصب حلال صيد حلال ثم أحرم الغاصب والصيد في يده لزمه إرساله وضمان قيمته للمغصوب منه، فلو لم يفعل ودفعه إلى المغصوب منه حتى برئ من الضمان له كان عليه الجزاء وقد أساء وهذا لغز؛ يقال غاصب يجب عليه عدم الرد بل إذا فعل يجب به الضمان فلو أحرم المغصوب منه ثم دفعه إليه فعلى كل واحد منهما الجزاء.
Chapter: If a Muhrim kills game and it gives birth, he does not guarantee the offspring. And taking... And indeed the sale is invalid (batil) and not merely voidable (fasid) because game with respect to a Muhrim is essentially prohibited, by His statement: 'And forbidden to you is game of the land as long as you are in a state of ihram' [al-Ma'idah 5:96]. He added the prohibition to the essence, so it indicates the removal of value in his right, like wine for a Muslim. And its summary is removing the essence from being permissible for all transactions, so dealing with it is futile, so it is intrinsically repugnant and thus invalidates, whether both are Muhrim or one of them. For this reason, the author made it absolute: it indicates that the sale of a Muhrim is invalid even if the buyer is halal, and that purchase is invalid even if the seller is halal. As for the penalty, it is only upon the Muhrim; so even if the seller is halal and the buyer is Muhrim, the buyer alone is liable. Based on this, every transaction: if he gifts game, then if both are Muhrim, each is liable for a penalty; if one of them is Muhrim, he alone is liable. And if two persons trade game while in the state of halal, then they or one of them become Muhrim, and then the buyer finds a defect in it, he may seek compensation for the decrease but cannot return it. And based on this, if a halal person usurps game from a halal owner, then the usurper becomes Muhrim while the game is in his hand, he must release it and guarantee its value to the owner. If he does not do so and instead hands it over to the owner from whom it was taken, thus becoming free from the guarantee, then he incurs the penalty and has done wrong. And this is a puzzle: it is said that a usurper must not return it, but if he does, he incurs liability. If the owner becomes Muhrim and then the usurper gives it to him, then each one of them is liable for a penalty.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage begins with a ruling from the matn: if a Muhrim kills game and it gives birth, he is not liable for the offspring. The commentary then expands on the invalidity of selling game while in ihram. The proof is from Quran 5:96, which prohibits 'game of the land' to a Muhrim. Because the prohibition is attached to the essence ('ayn) of the game, it removes its monetary value (taqawwum) for the Muhrim, making any transaction futile and thus batil (void) rather than fasid (voidable). This applies whether one or both parties are Muhrim. The author (al-Marghinani) makes it absolute: sale by a Muhrim is invalid even if the buyer is halal, and purchase by a Muhrim is invalid even if the seller is halal. The penalty (jaza') for the game is only on the Muhrim, so if a halal person sells game to a Muhrim, only the buyer incurs the penalty. This principle extends to gifts and other transactions. The passage also discusses a scenario where two halal persons trade game, then one or both become Muhrim, and the buyer later finds a defect: he can claim compensation for the decrease in value but cannot return the game, because the sale was invalid from inception. Finally, a case of usurpation (ghasb): if a halal person usurps game and then becomes Muhrim, he must release the game (because it is prohibited to possess) and guarantee its value to the owner. If he instead returns it to the owner (which is prohibited), he incurs the penalty. A puzzle highlights that if the owner becomes Muhrim after receiving the game, both incur penalties—a subtle point of fiqh.

Key Terms
محرم العين (muharram al-'ayn): Prohibited in its essence; the game itself is prohibited for a Muhrim, not just its use.
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty or compensation for killing or harming game while in ihram, typically by offering an equivalent animal or its value.
باطل (batil): Void; a contract that is fundamentally invalid and produces no legal effects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the sale of game by a Muhrim batil (void) rather than fasid (voidable)?
A) Because the prohibition on hunting is only on the act, not the game itself.
B) Because the game is considered 'ayn mahrum (essentially prohibited) for a Muhrim, thus it has no monetary value.
C) Because the sale is made without proper offer and acceptance.
D) Because only the buyer must be a Muhrim for the sale to be batil.

Key Takeaway
The sale of game by a Muhrim is batil because the game is essentially prohibited for them, stripping it of legal value, as proven by Quran 5:96.

The Ruling on Game Taken from the Haram: Offspring and Jaza'
Ruling on liability for offspring when a deer is taken from the Haram and jaza' is paid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for offspring of a deer taken from the Haram after paying jaza', and distinguish between cases of ability and inability to return the animal.

Core Idea
Jaza' for Haram game removes liability for offspring only if the taker is unable to return it.

When game is taken from the Haram, it retains legal protection until returned. But what happens if the animal gives birth after the taker pays compensation? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the taker's ability to return the animal. This lesson unpacks a nuanced ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary, focusing on when jaza' suffices and when it does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and rule
What is the initial liability when a deer is taken from the Haram? The matn states both mother and offspring are guaranteed.
2
Trace the effect of paying jaza'
After paying jaza', the offspring are not guaranteed. The substitute (jaza') replaces the original, ending protection.
3
Examine the distinction of ability
Fath al-Qadir refines: if the taker is able to return the deer, paying jaza' does not expiate; only if unable does it suffice.
This distinction is crucial for the practical outcome.
4
Apply the distinction to ownership
After paying jaza' (when unable), the taker owns the deer but with a base ownership (milk khabith), making eating makruh tahrimi.
5
Note the ruling on increase
If the deer's value increases before paying jaza', the increase is guaranteed; after payment, it is not.
This applies to attached increases like fatness or hair.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن أخرج ظبية الحرم فولدت فاتا ضمنهما فإن أدى جزاءها فولدت لا يضمن الولد) لأن الصيد بعد الإخراج من الحرم بقي مستحق إلا من شرعاً ولهذا وجب رده إلى مأمنه، وهذه صفة شرعية فتسري إلى الولد فإن أدى جزاءها ثم ولدت ليس عليه جزاء الولد لأن بعد أداء الجزاء لم تبق آمنة لأن وصول الخلف كوصول الأصل، ولهذا يملكها الذي أخرجها بعد أداء الجزاء، ولهذا لو ذبحها لم تكن ميتة لكنه مكروه ـ كذا قالوا ـ وقد بحث فيه المحقق في فتح القدير فقال : والذي يقتضيه النظر أن أداء الجزاء إن كان حال القدرة على إعادة مأمنها بالرد إلى المأمن لا يقع كفارة ولا يحل بعده التعرض له بل حرمة التعرض إليها قائمة، وإن كان حال العجز عنه بأن هربت في الحل بعد ما أخرجها إليه خرج به عن عهدتها فلا يضمن ما يحدث بعد التكفير من أولادها وله أن يصطادها، وهذا لأن والمثل معاً.

هـ.

وقد
سبب
المتوجه قبل العجز عن تأمينها إنما هو خطاب الرد إلى المأمن ولا يزال متوجهاً ما كان قادراً لأن سقوط الأمر إنما هو بفعل المأمور به ما لم يعجز ولم يوجه، فإذا عجز توجد خطاب الجزاء، وقد صرح بأن الأخذ ليس سبباً للضمان بل القتل بالنص فالتكفير قبله واقع قبل السبب فلا يقع إلا نفلاً فإذا ماتت بعد أداء هذا الجزاء لزم الجزاء لأنه الآن تعلق خطاب الجزاء. هذا الذي أدين الله به وأقول : يكره اصطيادها إذا أدى الجزاء بعد الهرب ثم ظفر بها بشبهة كون دوام العجز شرط إجزاء الكفارة إلا إذا اصطادها ليردها إلى الحرم ا هـ . يقال : إنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون المخرج محرماً أو حلالاً، فإن كان محرماً فلا شك أن الضمان قد وجد وهو التعرض للصيد فإن الآية وإن أفادت حرمة القتل أفادت السنة حرمة التعرض قتلاً أو غيره ولهذا وجب الضمان بالدلالة وليست قتلاً وقد صرحوا كما قدمناه بأن المحرم إذا جرح صيداً فكفر ثم مات فإنه لا يلزمه كفارة أخرى لأنه أدى بعد السبب وليس قتلاً، وإن كان المخرج حلالاً فالنص الحديثي أفاد حرمة التنفير كما قدمناه بقوله «ولا ينفر صيدها ولم يخص القتل. والمراد من التنفير التعرض له فإنه حرام كالقتل وإن كان لا يجب عليه بالدلالة شيء فإذا أخرجها فقد اتصل فعله بها فوجد سبب الضمان فجاز التكفير، فإذا أدى الجزاء ملكها ملكاً خبيثاً ولهذا قالوا يكره أكلها وهي عند إطلاقهم منصرفة إلى الكراهة التحريمية فدل أنه يجب ردها إلى الحرم بعد أداء الجزاء، ولو كان القتل عيناً سبباً للجزاء لم يجب الجزاء بإخراجها وعدم قدرته على ردها إلى الحرم ،بهربها، فالظاهر ما ذهب إليه أئمتنا. وأشار المصنف رحمه الله تعالى بحكم الزيادة المنفصلة إلى الزيادة المتصلة كالسمن والشعر فإن أخرج حلال ظبية الحرم فازدادت قيمتها من بدن أو شعر ثم ماتت، فإن لم يؤد جزاءها قبل موتها فالزيادة مضمونة وإن أدى جزاءها قبل موتها فهي غير مضمونة لأنه انعدم أثر الفعل بالتكفير حتى لو أنشأ الفعل فيها لم يضمن. ولو أخرجها من الحرم فباعها أو ذبحها أو أكلها جاز البيع والأكل ويكره وحكم الزيادة عند المشتري قبل التكفير وبعده على ما ذكرناه قبل الشراء. كذا في المحيط. وهو كما قدمناه يفيد أن الإخراج من الحرم لما كان سبباً للضمان كان سبباً للملك ولو لم يؤد الجزاء. والظبية الأنثى من الظباء والله سبحانه وتعالى الموفق للصواب وإليه المرجع وا والمآب .
His statement: (Whoever takes a female deer from the Haram and it gives birth, then both are guaranteed, and if he pays its penalty then it gives birth, he does not guarantee the offspring) because the game after being taken out of the Haram remained protected by the Law, and for this reason it must be returned to its safe place, and this is a legal quality that extends to the offspring. If he pays its penalty and then it gives birth, he is not liable for the offspring's penalty because after paying the penalty it is no longer protected, since the substitute (al-khalaf) reaches the same status as the original (al-asl). For this reason, the one who took it owns it after paying the penalty. For this reason, if he slaughters it, it is not carrion but it is disliked (makruh) — thus they said. And the investigator in Fath al-Qadir discussed it and said: What consideration requires is that paying the penalty while able to return it to its safe place by returning it to the safe place does not count as expiation, and after it it is not permissible to harm it; rather, the prohibition of harming it remains. But if he is unable to do so, as when it fled to the halal (outside Haram) after he brought it out, then he is discharged from its responsibility, and he does not guarantee what occurs after the expiation of its offspring, and he may hunt it. This is because... and the like together. I have not seen the answer organized, so I organized it in my saying: No, this halal person sold game that was hunted by a Muhrim, so what protected his ihram and what he tended? And he destroyed the game sold, side by side, liable for value and the like together. End quote. I say: But in it, the sold item is fasid; the buyer owns it by possession, so the owner here is the buyer, not the seller. His statement: (If he does not do so and hands it over to the owner from whom it was taken, etc.) I say: The obligation of the penalty in this scenario is problematic according to the statement of the text: 'And if a halal person takes game and then becomes Muhrim, he guarantees it when he sends it' because the sender has destroyed it, so he guarantees it. For what has passed. And the obligation on him is to refrain from harming, and he can do so by leaving it in his house; if he cuts off his hand from it, he becomes a transgressor. End quote. His statement: And the address before inability to secure it is only the command to return to the safe place, and it remains binding as long as he is able, because the obligation is only dropped by performing the commanded act unless he is unable and so the command is not addressed. When he becomes unable, the command of penalty arises. And he stated that taking is not a cause for guarantee; rather, killing by the text. So expiation before it occurs before the cause, so it only falls as a supererogatory act. If it dies after paying this penalty, the penalty becomes due because now the penalty command is attached. This is what I believe in before Allah. And I say: It is disliked to hunt it if he paid the penalty after it fled and then captured it, due to the suspicion that the continuity of inability is a condition for the validity of the expiation, unless he hunts it to return it to the Haram. End quote. It is said: It is not free from either the one who takes it being a Muhrim or halal. If he is a Muhrim, then there is no doubt that the guarantee exists, which is harming the game, for the verse indicates the prohibition of killing, and the Sunnah indicates the prohibition of harming, killing or otherwise, and therefore guarantee is due by indication, even if it is not killing. And they have stated, as we have mentioned, that if a Muhrim wounds game and then expiates and it dies, he is not liable for another expiation, because he expiated after the cause and it is not killing. If the one who takes it is halal, then the hadith text indicates the prohibition of frightening, as we have mentioned with his statement: 'And do not frighten its game.' And he did not specify killing. And the meaning of frightening is harming it, for it is forbidden like killing, even if nothing is due by indication. So when he takes it out, his act is connected to it, and thus the cause of guarantee exists, so expiation is permissible. When he pays the penalty, he owns it with a base ownership, and therefore they said it is disliked to eat it, and when they are absolute, it refers to tahrimi dislike (makruh tahrimi). It indicates that it must be returned to the Haram after paying the penalty. And if killing were specifically the cause of the penalty, the penalty would not be required by taking it out and not being able to return it to the Haram by its fleeing. So what is apparent is what our imams went to. And the author Ibn al-Humam indicated by the ruling of separate increase (al-ziyada al-munfasila) to the attached increase (al-ziyada al-muttasila) like fatness and hair. So if a halal person takes a female deer from the Haram and its value increases due to body or hair, then it dies, then if he did not pay its penalty before its death, the increase is guaranteed; but if he paid its penalty before its death, it is not guaranteed, because the effect of the act is eliminated by expiation, so even if he initiates an act in it he is not liable. And if he takes it out of the Haram and sells it, slaughters it, or eats it, the sale and eating are permissible but disliked. And the ruling of the increase with the buyer before expiation and after it is as we mentioned before purchase. Thus in al-Muhit. And it is as we have presented: that taking out from the Haram, since it is a cause for guarantee, is a cause for ownership even if he did not pay the penalty. And al-zabyah is the female of the deer. And Allah Almighty is the grantor of success, and to Him is the return and the final destination.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a matn line from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding taking a female deer from the Haram. The matn states: if someone takes a female deer from the Haram and it gives birth, both mother and offspring are guaranteed (i.e., must be returned or compensated). If he pays the penalty (jaza') for the deer and then it gives birth, he is not liable for the offspring. The commentary explains that when an animal is taken from the Haram, it remains protected by the Law (mustahaqq al-aman), so it must be returned. This quality extends to its offspring. However, once the penalty is paid, the animal is no longer considered 'protected' because the substitute (the penalty) replaces the original. Thus, the person who took it becomes owner (though the ownership is 'base' or 'vile', making it makruh to eat/e). A detailed discussion from Fath al-Qadir is presented: if the person pays the penalty while still able to return the animal to the Haram, it does not count as expiation (kaffarah), and the prohibition against harming remains; if he is unable to return it (e.g., it fled), then paying the penalty discharges him, and he may even hunt it later. The author of the commentary (Ibn al-Humam) then shares a poetic summary of a related ruling: a halal person sells game that was hunted by a Muhrim—the seller is liable for value and mithl (like) together. He critiques that the buyer actually becomes owner by possession in a fasid sale. The discussion then returns to the deer: the obligation of returning the deer remains as long as one is able; when unable, the penalty becomes due. If the taker is a Muhrim, the guarantee is established by harming the game (even without killing). If the taker is halal, the hadith 'Do not frighten its game' indicates prohibition of any disturbance. Taking the deer out connects the act to it, creating the cause for guarantee, so paying the penalty is valid. After paying, the person owns it but with a base ownership (milk khabith), making eating makruh tahrimi, and it must be returned to the Haram. The passage concludes with a ruling on incremental increases: if the deer's value increases (e.g., fatness) before penalty, the increase is guaranteed; if after penalty, it is not. Also, taking the deer out is a cause for both guarantee and ownership, even without paying penalty.

Key Terms
الظبية (al-zabyah): Female deer; the text uses it as an example of game from the Haram.
مستحق الأمن (mustahaqq al-aman): Deserving of protection; after taking it from the Haram, the game still has legal inviolability.
ملك خبيث (milk khabith): Base ownership; ownership acquired through prohibited means, allowing possession but making use disliked (makruh tahrimi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The jaza' is valid and the deer becomes his property.
B) The jaza' does not count as expiation and the deer must be returned.
C) The jaza' is valid only if he also returns the deer.
D) The deer's offspring become free from liability.

Key Takeaway
Paying jaza' for Haram game only removes liability for offspring when the taker is unable to return the animal; otherwise, return is still wajib.

The Obligation to Release Game in Ihram and Ruling on Its Sale
Critical note on two fiqh rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what 'tark al-ta'arrud' requires of a Muhrim holding game, and explain why selling game taken out of the Haram is considered weak in the school.

Core Idea
Refraining from harming game does not require release; keeping it safely suffices. Selling outside Haram is weak.

This lesson examines a critical note from al-Bahr al-Raiq that refines two points in Hanafi fiqh. First, the meaning of 'tark al-ta'arrud' (refraining from harming) when a person in ihram has game; second, the ruling on selling game after taking it out of the Haram. The note challenges a simplistic reading and urges careful consideration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
Recognize that the note addresses two separate rulings: (a) the obligation of the usurper who enters ihram with game, and (b) the permissibility of selling game taken out of the Haram.
Both are marked by the author's call to 'consider' (tأمل).
2
Analyze the first point: meaning of 'tark al-ta'arrud'
The text clarifies that 'refraining from harming' does not require release; the person may keep the game in his house as long as he does not harm it.
This is a refinement of a broader obligation.
3
Understand the second point: sale of game outside Haram
The ruling that such a sale is permissible is cited, but the note mentions that it is considered 'weak' (da'if) according to al-Nahr.
This implies the authoritative position may differ.
4
Reflect on the author's call to 'consider'
The phrase 'tأمل' (consider) indicates a point of scholarly nuance or unfinished debate, prompting further research.
Such devices are common in Hanafi super-commentaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والواجب عليه ترك التعرض الخ صريح في أنه لا يلزمه إرساله من يده لإمكاه تخليته في بيته فهلا كان دفع الغاصب مثل تخلية المالك فليتأمل . قوله : ( ولو أخرجها من الحرم فباعها أو ذبحها الخ) تقدم عن النهر أنه ضعيف تأمل.
And the obligation on him to refrain from harming... is explicit that he is not required to release it from his hand because he can keep it in his house. So why is the usurper's returning it not like the owner's keeping it? Let this be considered. His statement: (And if he takes it out of the Haram and sells it or slaughters it, etc.) It has been mentioned from al-Nahr that it is weak. Consider.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a short critical note (hashiya-style) on two points. First, it comments on the earlier statement that a person who wrongfully took game (ghasb) and became Muhrim must 'refrain from harming' (ترك التعرض). The note argues that 'refraining from harming' does not necessarily mean releasing the animal from his hand; he may keep it in his house as long as he does not harm it. The note questions why, in the earlier puzzle, returning the game to the original owner (who becomes Muhrim) incurs a penalty, when simply keeping it would be permissible. The phrase 'let it be considered' indicates the author is raising a subtle point for reflection. Second, it refers to the ruling that if a person takes a deer out of the Haram and then sells, slaughters, or eats it, that is permissible but disliked. The note cites al-Nahr (likely a reference to the work 'al-Nahr' by Ibn al-Humam or a commentary) that this ruling is 'weak' (da'if), implying that the authoritative position may be different. The reader is asked to 'consider' (tأمل) the matter carefully.

Key Terms
ترك التعرض (tark al-ta'arrud): Refraining from harming the game; not actively pursuing or damaging it.
تأمل (ta'ammul): Reflection; the author asks the reader to consider the point carefully.
ضعيف (da'if): Weak; referring to a ruling that is not strongly supported and may not be relied upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the note, what is the status of the ruling that selling game outside the Haram is permissible?
A) It is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
B) It is considered weak (da'if).
C) It is forbidden outright.
D) It is recommended.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, refraining from harming game while in ihram does not necessitate release; keeping it safely suffices. Moreover, the ruling on selling game outside the Haram is considered weak, urging caution.

Rulings on a Muhrim's Interaction with Game and Compensation
Discussion of ruling when a muhrim causes game to flee and pays fidyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim's ownership of game after paying compensation and explain why it is makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Paying fidyah for causing game to flee creates 'evil ownership' — the game must be returned to the Haram, not consumed.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Shaykh Zayla'i addresses a nuanced scenario: a muhrim who causes game to flee, pays compensation, then later catches it. Is the game now his property? Can he eat it? The answer reveals a key Hanafi principle about the relationship between compensation (jaza') and ownership, and the distinction between a muhrim and a non-muhrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage discusses a muhrim (or non-muhrim) causing game to flee from the Haram, paying compensation, then catching it. The ruling given by the author: it is makruh tahrimi to hunt it, except to return it to the Haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith 'لا ينفر صيدها' (do not scare its game) and the Quranic verse on hunting (al-Ma'idah 5:95). The hadith extends the prohibition from killing to scaring (tanfir).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of scaring is derived from the hadith; exposure to game is equated to scaring. The author argues that exposure (ta'arud) to game is prohibited like killing, but the guarantee (daman) is not triggered by exposure alone for a non-muhrim; only killing incurs a guarantee for him. However, if he removes the game from the Haram, he becomes liable and can pay compensation.
4
Determine the thamarah (practical consequence)
Once compensation is paid, the person owns the game but with 'evil ownership' (milk khabith), making consumption makruh tahrimi. The game must be returned to the Haram. This differs from the case where the game is killed; then the compensation is for the killing, and ownership is not acquired.
Note: The author distinguishes between a muhrim (for whom exposure itself incurs guarantee) and a non-muhrim (for whom guarantee arises only upon actual removal from the Haram).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً وقد سبب المتوجه قبل العجز عن تأمينها إنما هو خطاب الرد إلى المأمن ولا يزال متوجهاً ما كان قادراً لأن سقوط الأمر إنما هو بفعل المأمور به ما لم يعجز ولم يوجه، فإذا عجز توجد خطاب الجزاء، وقد صرح بأن الأخذ ليس سبباً للضمان بل القتل بالنص فالتكفير قبله واقع قبل السبب فلا يقع إلا نفلاً فإذا ماتت بعد أداء هذا الجزاء لزم الجزاء لأنه الآن تعلق خطاب الجزاء. هذا الذي أدين الله به وأقول : يكره اصطيادها إذا أدى الجزاء بعد الهرب ثم ظفر بها بشبهة كون دوام العجز شرط إجزاء الكفارة إلا إذا اصطادها ليردها إلى الحرم ا هـ . يقال : إنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون المخرج محرماً أو حلالاً، فإن كان محرماً فلا شك أن الضمان قد وجد وهو التعرض للصيد فإن الآية وإن أفادت حرمة القتل أفادت السنة حرمة التعرض قتلاً أو غيره ولهذا وجب الضمان بالدلالة وليست قتلاً وقد صرحوا كما قدمناه بأن المحرم إذا جرح صيداً فكفر ثم مات فإنه لا يلزمه كفارة أخرى لأنه أدى بعد السبب وليس قتلاً، وإن كان المخرج حلالاً فالنص الحديثي أفاد حرمة التنفير كما قدمناه بقوله «ولا ينفر صيدها ولم يخص القتل. والمراد من التنفير التعرض له فإنه حرام كالقتل وإن كان لا يجب عليه بالدلالة شيء فإذا أخرجها فقد اتصل فعله بها فوجد سبب الضمان فجاز التكفير، فإذا أدى الجزاء ملكها ملكاً خبيثاً ولهذا قالوا يكره أكلها وهي عند إطلاقهم منصرفة إلى الكراهة التحريمية فدل أنه يجب ردها إلى الحرم بعد أداء الجزاء، ولو كان القتل عيناً سبباً للجزاء لم يجب الجزاء بإخراجها وعدم قدرته على ردها إلى الحرم ،بهربها، فالظاهر ما ذهب إليه أئمتنا. وأشار المصنف رحمه الله تعالى بحكم الزيادة المنفصلة إلى الزيادة المتصلة كالسمن والشعر فإن أخرج حلال ظبية الحرم فازدادت قيمتها من بدن أو شعر ثم ماتت، فإن لم يؤد جزاءها قبل موتها فالزيادة مضمونة وإن أدى جزاءها قبل موتها فهي غير مضمونة لأنه انعدم أثر الفعل بالتكفير حتى لو أنشأ الفعل فيها لم يضمن. ولو أخرجها من الحرم فباعها أو ذبحها أو أكلها جاز البيع والأكل ويكره وحكم الزيادة عند المشتري قبل التكفير وبعده على ما ذكرناه قبل الشراء. كذا في المحيط. وهو كما قدمناه يفيد أن الإخراج من الحرم لما كان سبباً للضمان كان سبباً للملك ولو لم يؤد الجزاء. والظبية الأنثى من الظباء والله سبحانه وتعالى الموفق للصواب وإليه المرجع وا والمآب . والواجب عليه ترك التعرض الخ صريح في أنه لا يلزمه إرساله من يده لإمكاه تخليته في بيته فهلا كان دفع الغاصب مثل تخلية المالك فليتأمل . قوله : ( ولو أخرجها من الحرم فباعها أو ذبحها الخ) تقدم عن النهر أنه ضعيف تأمل.
Chapter: If a muhrim kills game. And the directed (address) before inability to secure it is only the address of returning to safety, and it remains directed as long as he is able, because the falling away of the command is only by doing the commanded thing as long as he is not unable and has not been directed. So when he becomes unable, the address of compensation occurs. And it has been explicitly stated that taking is not a cause for guarantee, but rather killing by text, so the expiation before it occurs before the cause, so it only occurs as a supererogatory (nafl). So if it dies after performing this compensation, the compensation is required because now the address of compensation is attached. This is what I hold as my religion and I say: It is disliked (makruh) to hunt it if he has paid the compensation after its escape and then catches it, due to the suspicion that the continuity of inability is a condition for the sufficiency of the expiation, unless he hunts it to return it to the Haram. It is said: It is unavoidable; either the remover is a muhrim or a non-muhrim. If he is a muhrim, there is no doubt that guarantee has occurred, which is the exposure to game, for the verse, even if it indicates the prohibition of killing, the Sunnah indicates the prohibition of exposure whether by killing or otherwise, and for this reason guarantee is obligated by indication, and it is not killing. And they have stated, as we have presented, that if a muhrim wounds game and then expiates and then it dies, he is not obligated another expiation because he performed after the cause and it is not killing. And if the remover is a non-muhrim, the hadith text indicates the prohibition of scaring as we have presented with his saying: 'and do not scare its game' and he did not specify killing. The meaning of scaring is exposure to it, for it is prohibited like killing, even if nothing is obligatory upon him by indication. So when he removes it, his action has connected with it, and the cause of guarantee is found, so expiation is permissible. So when he pays the compensation, he owns it with an evil ownership, and for this reason they said it is disliked to eat it, and their absolute usage refers to prohibitive dislike (karahah tahrimiyyah). So it indicates that it must be returned to the Haram after paying the compensation. And if killing were exactly the cause for compensation, compensation would not be obligatory by removing it and his inability to return it to the Haram due to its escape. So the apparent is what our imams held. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) indicated by the ruling of detached increase to the connected increase like fat and hair. So if a non-muhrim removes a female gazelle from the Haram and its value increases in body or hair and then it dies, if he did not pay its compensation before its death, the increase is guaranteed; if he paid its compensation before its death, it is not guaranteed because the effect of the action has been nullified by expiation, such that if he creates the action in it, he is not liable. And if he removes it from the Haram and sells it, slaughters it, or eats it, the sale and eating are permissible but disliked. And the ruling of the increase with the purchaser before expiation and after is as we mentioned before purchase. Thus in al-Muhit. And it is as we have presented: removing from the Haram, since it was a cause for guarantee, was a cause for ownership even if he did not pay the compensation. And 'al-zabyah' (female gazelle) is the female of gazelles. And Allah, the Exalted, is the granter of success to what is correct, and to Him is the return and the abode. And what is obligatory upon him is to refrain from exposure... It is explicit that he is not required to release it from his hand because it is possible to confine it in his house. So why is the repelling of the usurper not like the vacating of the owner? So let it be pondered. His statement: 'And if he removes it from the Haram and sells it or slaughters it etc.' has been previously mentioned from al-Nahr that it is weak. Contemplate.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the rulings related to a muhrim or non-muhrim who causes game to escape from the Haram. The author begins by addressing a prior statement about the nature of the address to return the game to safety. He then gives his own fatwa: it is makruh tahrimi to hunt the game after paying compensation for its escape, unless the intention is to return it to the Haram. He then examines two scenarios: if the remover is a muhrim, guarantee is established by exposure itself, even if not killing; if a non-muhrim, the hadith 'do not scare its game' makes scaring (tanfir) prohibited like killing, but only killing incurs a guarantee; however, if he removes it, he is liable and can pay compensation, after which he owns it with 'evil ownership' (milk khabith), hence eating is makruh tahrimi and it must be returned to the Haram. The author then discusses the ruling on increase (ziyadah) in value: if the animal increases in body or hair after removal and then dies, if compensation was paid before death, the increase is not guaranteed; if not, it is guaranteed. Finally, he mentions that if a non-muhrim sells, slaughters, or eats the animal, it is permissible but disliked, and the increase is ruled similarly. The passage ends with a note that some consider the view in al-Nahr weak.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
جزاء (jaza'): Compensation or expiation for harming game, typically by slaughtering a similar animal in the Haram.
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): A degree of dislike bordering on prohibition; acting upon it is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, if a non-muhrim removes a gazelle from the Haram and pays compensation, what is the ruling on eating it?
A) Halal and recommended
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Haram without exception
D) Permissible but must be slaughtered

Key Takeaway
Paying compensation for causing game to flee from the Haram does not make the meat halal; ownership is 'evil' and the game must be returned to the Haram.
