Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Combining Two Hajj Ihrams on Yawm al-Nahr
Commentary on matn regarding combining two Hajj ihrams on Yawm al-Nahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining two Hajj ihrams on Yawm al-Nahr and identify the mufta bihi position regarding the requirement of a dam.

Core Idea
Combining two Hajj ihrams is not prohibited but may require a dam; the three imams differ on when.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a practical question: can a pilgrim who has already entered ihram for Hajj perform a second ihram on the day of Nahr? While some earlier texts like al-Hidayah declare it haram, the Hanafi school's apparent narration permits it. However, the three eponymous imams differ on the necessity of a compensatory dam (dam). This lesson dissects their arguments and clarifies the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling from the matn
From the matn: If someone performs ihram for Hajj, then for another on the day of Nahr, if he shaves (halq) for the first, the second is binding without dam; otherwise, binding with dam.
The matn itself appears to require dam in a specific case.
2
Distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the dam
Abu Hanifa holds that if the second ihram is before halq, a dam is required absolutely, whether he shaves afterwards or not. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict the dam to the case where he actually shaves for the first.
3
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
For Abu Hanifa, if he shaves, he has trespassed against the second ihram; if he does not, he delayed the ritual. For the Sahibayn, delay alone does not warrant a dam; the act of shaving causes the violation.
Note also that Muhammad further holds that only one ihram is binding, so no dam for combining.
4
Determine the relied-upon position and its practical consequence
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that combining two Hajj ihrams is not disliked, and a dam is required only if one shaves for the first before the second ihram. This follows al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Muhit.
Practical consequence: Hanafis may perform two Hajjs in successive years by deferring the second's performance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب مجاوزة الميقات بغير إحرام
۹۱
مضى عليهما صح وعليه دم ومن أحرم بحج ثم بآخر يوم النحر فإن حلق في الأول
في وجوب الدم، وأما في وجوب العمرة فمقيد بما إذا لم يحج من سنته، أما إذا حج من سنته فلا عمرة عليه لأن وجوب العمرة مع الحج إنما هو لكونه في معنى فائت الحج، وإذا حج من سنته فليس في معناه كالمحصر إذا تحلل ثم حج في تلك السنة لا تجب العمرة عليه بخلاف ما إذا تحولت السنة. ووقع في نسخة الزيلعي الشارح أنه أبدل العمرة بالدم فقال : إذا حج من سنته ينبغي أن لا يجب عليه الدم. وهو سبق قلم كما لا يخفى. والرفض الترك وهو من بابي طلب وضرب. كذا في المغرب.
قوله : ( ومن أحرم بحج ثم بآخر يوم النحر فإن حلق في الأول لزمه الآخر ولا دم وإلا لزم وعليه دم قصر أو لا ومن فرغ من عمرته إلا التقصير فأحرم بأخرى لزمه دم بيان للجمع بين إحرامين لشيئين متحدين، وصرح في الهداية بأنه بدعة، وإفراط في غاية البيان فقال : إن الجمع بين الإحرامين لحجتين أو لعمرتين حرام لأنه بدعة .اهـ. وهو سهو لما في المحيط : والجمع بين إحرامي الحج لا يكره في ظاهر الرواية لأن في العمرة إنما كره الجمع بين الإحرامين لأنه يصير جامعاً بينهما في الفعل لأنه يؤديهما في سنة واحدة، وفي الحج لا يصير . جامعاً بينهما في الأداء في سنة واحدة فلا يكره .اهـ. فإذا أحرم بحجة ووقف بعرفات ثم أحرم بأخرى يوم النحر فإن الثانية تلزمه مطلقاً لإمكان الأداء لأن الإحرام الثاني إنما يرتفض لتعذر الأداء ولا تعذر هنا في الأداء لأن إحرامه انصرف إلى حجة في السنة القابلة، فإن كان الإحرام الثاني بعد الحلق للأول فلا دم عليه لأنه أحرم بالثانية بعد التحلل من الأولى فلم يكن جامعاً، وإن كان قبل الحلق لزمه دم عند أبي حنيفة مطلقاً لأنه إن حلق للأولى فقد جنى على إحرام الثانية، وإن كان نسكاً في إحرام الأولى وإن لم يحلق فقد أخر النسك عن وقته وهما يخصان الوجوب بما إذا حلق لأنهما لا يوجبان بالتأخير شيئاً. وبهذا علم أن المراد بالتقصير في قوله «قصر (أولاً) الحلق وإنما اختاره اتباعاً للجامع الصغير كما في غاية البيان، أو ليصير الحكم جارياً في المرأة لأن التقصير عام في الرجل والمرأة كما في
مه
إحرامي حجتين فصاعداً إما أن يكوناً معاً أو على التعاقب أو على التراخي، وعلى الثالث إما أن يكون بعد الحلق للأول أو قبله، وإذا كان قبله فإما أن يفوته الحج من عامه أو لا قوله : (وهو سهو) قال في النهر: ليس من السهو في شيء بل مبني على رواية الأصل ا هـ. أي رواية عدم الفرق بين الحجتين والعمرتين كما يأتي، وكيف يكون سهواً وقد قال في التتارخانية : الجمع بين إحرام الحج والعمرة بدعة. وفي الجامع الصغير العتابي : حرام لأنه من أكبر الكبائر. هكذا روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قوله : (فإن الثانية تلزمه مطلقاً أي سواء أحرم للثانية قبل الحلق أو بعده قوله : (وإن كان قبل الحلق الخ) قال في اللباب : وإن كان قبل الحلق عليه دم الجمع وهو دم جبر ويلزمه دم آخر، سواء حلق للأول بعد الإحرام للثاني أو لا، ولو حلق بعد أيام النحر فعليه دم ثالث ا هـ . ولزوم دم الجمع على إحدى الروايتين كما سينبه عليه المؤلف قريباً قوله : (الزمه دم عند أبي حنيفة مطلقاً) أي
هـ.

۹۲
كتاب الحج باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام
العناية . وإنما لزم الدم فيما إذا أحرم بعد رم بعمرة بعد أفعال الأولى قبل الحلق لأنه جمع بينهما، وقد تقدم أنه مكروه في العمرتين دون الحجتين فلذا فرق في المختصر بين الحج والعمرة فأوجب في العمرة دماً للجمع بين العمرتين ولم يوجبه في الحج لأنه لو أوجبه لأوجب دمين فيما إذا أحرم بالثاني قبل الحلق للأول دم لما ذكرناه سبقاً ودم للجمع، وبه قال بعض المشايخ اتباعاً لرواية الأصل، وما في المختصر اتباع للجامع الصغير فإنه أوجب دماً واحداً للحج ، وقد علمت فيما سبق عن المحيط أن الفرق بينهما ظاهر الرواية، وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه لا يتم لأن كونه يتمكن من أداء العمرة الثانية لا يوجب الجمع فعلاً فاستويا، فالأوجه أنه ليس فيه إلا رواية الوجوب اهـ. وقيد بكونه أحرم للثاني يوم النحر لأنه لو أحرم بالثاني بعرفات ليلاً أو نهاراً رفض الثانية وعليه دم للرفض، وعمرة وحجة من قابل عندهما لأنه كفائت الحج، وعند محمد لا يصح التزامه الثانية . ثم عند أبي يوسف ارتفض كما انعقد، وعند أبي حنيفة ارتفض بوقوفه بعرفة . كذا في المحيط وهو ظاهر فيما إذا أحرم بالثاني يوم عرفة أو ليلة النحر ولم يكن وقف نهاراً، وأما إذا أحرم ليلة النحر بعدما وقف نهاراً فينبغي أن يرتفض عند أبي حنيفة بالوقوف بالمزدلفة لا بعرفة لأنه سابق وسبب الترك إنما يكون متأخراً. وقيد بتراخي إحرام الثاني عن الأول لأنه إن أحرم بهما معاً أو على التعاقب لزماه عندهما، وعند محمد في المعية يلزمه إحداهما وفي التعاقب الأولى فقط، وإذا لزماه عندهما ارتفضت إحداهما ويثبت حكم الرفض. واختلفا في وقت الرفض، فعند أبي يوسف عقب صيرورته محرماً بلا مهلة وعند أبي حنيفة إذا شرع في الأعمال، وقيل إذا توجه سائراً، ونص في
وهو
،
ذلك
سواء حلق بعد ذلك أو لا قوله : (وهما يخصان الوجوب بما إذا حلق انظر هذا مع ما في النهر من أن لزوم الحج الآخر عندهما. وقال محمد : لا يصح . ثم رأيته في العناية قال: لكن يرد عليه شيء . أن المذكور من مذهب محمد في هذا الأصل أنه إذا جمع بين إحرامين إنما يلزمه أحدهما وهو المروي عن الإمام التمرتاشي والفوائد الظهيرية، وحينئذ ينبغي أن لا يلزمه دم وإن قصر لعدم لزوم الآخر، فإما أن يكون سهواً في نقل مذهب محمد ومذهبه كمذهبنا وإما أن يكون عنه في روايتان ا هـ. والله الحمد والمنة قوله : (فإنه أوجب دماً واحداً للحج قال في المعراج وفي الكافي : قيل لا خلاف بين الروايتين لأنه سكت في الجامع عن إيجاب الدم بسب الجمع وما نفاه. وقيل: بل فيه روايتان كما ذكر في جامع الكشاني ا.هـ. واستوجه في الفتح القول الأول كما يأتي. وفي العناية : وهذه المسألة أيضاً تدل على أن مذهب محمد في لزوم الإحرامين كمذهبهما وإلا لما لزم عنده شيء لأن الجمع غير متحقق لعدم لزوم أحدهما إلا إذا أراد بالجمع إدخال الإحرام على الإحرام وإن لم يلزم إلا أحدهما فيستقيم قوله : (وقد علمت الخ) فيه أن الأصل أيضاً من كتب ظاهر الرواية قوله : فينبغي أن يرتفض عند أبي حنيفة بالوقوف بالمزدلفة) قال في النهر لكن قياس ظاهر الرواية أي عن المبسوط أن يبطل بالمسير إليها قوله : (ودم عند أبي يوسف أي للجناية سوى دم الرفض قوله : (لزمه عمرتان وحجتان) عزاه في شرح اللباب إلى منسك الفارسي والطرابلسي والبحر العميق
الآتي
Book of Hajj, Chapter: Passing the Miqat without Ihram. 91. If it has passed over them, it is valid and upon him is a dam. And whoever performs ihram for Hajj then for another on the day of Nahr, if he shaves the head for the first, the latter becomes binding and no dam; otherwise it is binding and upon him is a dam, whether he shortens or not. And whoever finishes his Umrah except the taqsir and then performs ihram for another, upon him is a dam. This is an explanation of combining two ihrams for two unified things. And in al-Hidayah it is stated that it is a bid'ah and an excess in extreme clarity: 'Indeed combining two ihrams for two Hajjs or two Umrahs is haram because it is a bid'ah.' But this is an oversight, because in al-Muhit: 'Combining two ihrams for Hajj is not disliked in the apparent narration because in Umrah, combining two ihrams is disliked because one becomes combining them in action—performing them in one year—but in Hajj, he does not combine them in performance in one year, so it is not disliked.' So if one performs ihram for a Hajj and stands at Arafat, then performs ihram for another on the day of Nahr, that second one is binding absolutely due to the possibility of performance, because the second ihram is only rejected due to the impossibility of performance, and there is no impossibility here because his ihram is directed to a Hajj in the following year. If the second ihram is after shaving the head for the first, then no dam, because he performed ihram for the second after exiting ihram from the first, so he did not combine. If it was before shaving, then a dam is required according to Abu Hanifa absolutely, because if he shaves for the first, he has trespassed against the ihram of the second; and if it is a ritual act within the first ihram and he does not shave, then he has delayed the ritual from its time. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict the obligation to the case where he shaves, because they do not impose anything for delay. And from this it is known that what is meant by taqsir in his statement 'he shortens' (firstly) is shaving the head. He chose it in accordance with al-Jami' al-Saghir as in Ghayat al-Bayan, or so that the ruling applies to women because taqsir is common to men and women. So for two or more Hajj ihrams, either they are simultaneous, consecutive, or with delay. In the third case, either after shaving for the first or before it. If before it, then either he misses Hajj of that year or not. His statement: 'And it is an oversight.' In al-Nahr it is said: 'It is not an oversight at all, but based on the narration of the original.' That is, the narration of no difference between two Hajjs and two Umrahs. And how could it be an oversight when in al-TatarKhaniyya it is said: 'Combining the ihram of Hajj and Umrah is a bid'ah.' And in al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Attabi: 'It is haram because it is among the major sins.' Thus it is narrated from the Prophet (ﷺ). His statement: 'Indeed the second is binding absolutely' means whether he performed ihram for the second before shaving or after. His statement: 'And if it was before shaving etc.' In al-Lubab it is said: 'And if it was before shaving, upon him is the dam of combination, which is a compensatory dam, and another dam is required, whether he shaves for the first after the ihram for the second or not. And if he shaves after the days of Nahr, then a third dam is required.' And the obligation of the dam of combination is according to one of the two narrations, as the author will mention soon. His statement: 'a dam is required according to Abu Hanifa absolutely' means whether he shaves after that or not. His statement: 'And they restrict the obligation to the case where he shaves.' Look at this with what is in al-Nahr regarding the binding of the other Hajj according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?). And Muhammad said: 'It is not valid.' Then I saw in al-Inayah: 'But something is objected to it: That what is mentioned from the madhhab of Muhammad in this principle is that if he combines two ihrams, only one of them is binding, and this is narrated from Imam al-Tamartashi and al-Fawaid al-Zahiriyya. In that case, it should be that no dam is required even if he shortens, due to the non-binding of the other. So either it is an oversight in transmitting the madhhab of Muhammad, and his madhhab is like ours, or there are two narrations from him.' And praise be to Allah. His statement: 'Indeed he required one dam for Hajj.' In al-Mi'raj and al-Kafi it is said: 'It is said there is no difference between the two narrations because he was silent in al-Jami' about requiring a dam due to combination and did not negate it.' And it is said: 'Rather there are two narrations as mentioned in Jami' al-Kashani.' In al-Fath, the first opinion is considered preferable. And in al-Inayah: 'This issue also indicates that the madhhab of Muhammad regarding the binding of two ihrams is like theirs (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa), otherwise nothing would be binding according to him, because combination is not actualized due to non-binding of one of them, unless he intends by combination the entering of one ihram upon another even if only one is binding.' So his statement is correct. His statement: 'And you have known etc.' In it, the original is also from the books of the apparent narration. His statement: 'It should be rejected according to Abu Hanifa by standing at Muzdalifah.' In al-Nahr: 'But the analogy of the apparent narration i.e. from al-Mabsut is that it is invalidated by walking towards it.' His statement: 'And a dam according to Abu Yusuf' i.e. for the violation besides the dam of rejection. His statement: 'Two Umrahs and two Hajjs become binding.' In Sharh al-Lubab, it is attributed to Mansik al-Farisi, al-Tarabulsisi, and al-Bahr al-Amiq as will come.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding combining two ihrams for Hajj on the day of Nahr. The commentary primarily focuses on the intra-Hanafi dispute among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The matn states: if someone performs ihram for a Hajj, then later on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) performs another ihram for Hajj, if he performs the shaving (halq) for the first Hajj, the second ihram becomes binding and no dam is required; if he does not shave, the second is binding and a dam is required. The commentary clarifies that 'taqsir' (shortening) in the matn means shaving (halq) to include women. The author of al-Hidayah considered combining two Hajj ihrams as haram and bid'ah, but the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq, following al-Muhit, states that combining two Hajj ihrams is not disliked in the apparent narration because unlike Umrah, they are not performed in the same year. The dispute then centers on the requirement of a dam: Abu Hanifa holds that if the second ihram is before shaving, a dam is required absolutely. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict the dam to the case where one shaves, because delay alone does not warrant a dam in their view. Furthermore, there is a detailed discussion on the rejection (raft) of the second ihram according to each imam. Abu Hanifa considers the second ihram rejected by standing at Arafat or Muzdalifah; Abu Yusuf holds it is rejected immediately upon the second ihram; Muhammad holds that the second ihram does not even become valid. The passage also discusses the scenario where the second ihram is performed at Arafat night or day, and the ruling of dam for rejection. The author examines the apparent contradiction in al-Hidayah and reconciles it by noting multiple narrations. The practical consequence: a follower of the Hanafi school may combine two Hajj ihrams on different years, but must be careful about the timing of shaving and the required dam. The preferred position (mufta bihi) appears to be that combining two Hajj ihrams is not disliked per se, and the dam is required only if one shaves before completing the first Hajj activities.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihrām): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entered by reciting the talbiyah and wearing the ihram garments.
يوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice, when pilgrims perform the halq and other rites.
رفض (rafḍ): Rejection or abandonment of the ihram; the second ihram is considered rejected (murfad) if it cannot be performed due to time constraints.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as a compensation for certain violations during Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person performs ihram for a second Hajj on the day of Nahr before completing the first Hajj (i.e., before shaving/halq), what is the ruling regarding a dam?
A) No dam is required under any condition.
B) A dam is required absolutely, whether he shaves afterwards or not.
C) A dam is required only if he does not shave for the first.
D) A dam is required only if he shaves for the first.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits combining two Hajj ihrams; the key intra-school dispute is whether a dam is required unconditionally (Abu Hanifa) or only if shaving occurs (Sahibayn), with the relied-upon position being the latter.

Dam for Combining Two Umrahs vs Two Hajjs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dam for combining ihrams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dam for combining two Umrahs versus two Hajjs and identify the intra-madhhab dispute over the relied-upon narration.

Core Idea
Combining two Umrahs requires a dam; combining two Hajjs does not, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a specific ruling within the Hajj chapter: whether entering a second ihram while still in ihram requires a blood sacrifice (dam). The author explains the difference between Umrah and Hajj and highlights a dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding which narration is authoritative. Understanding this distinction is important for issuing correct fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? (Combining two Umrahs or two Hajjs by entering a second ihram before halq.) Determine the hukm for each.
The key act is 'idafat al-ihram' (adding a second ihram).
2
Locate the underlying principle
Why is combining Umrahs makruh but not combining Hajjs? The passage states the difference is based on whether the act is makruh.
Makruh acts in ihram often require compensation (dam).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some Hanafi mashayikh follow a narration (riwayat al-asl) that requires a dam for combining two Hajjs as well, while others (followers of al-Jami' al-Saghir) require dam only for Umrah.
The dispute is about which narration is zahir al-riwaya.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Bahr al-Raiq favors the view of al-Fath al-Qadir that only the obligation for Umrah is authentic. Thus, the relied-upon position is that dam is wajib only for combining two Umrahs.
Tarjih is based on later authorities and internal consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام
العناية . وإنما لزم الدم فيما إذا أحرم بعد رم بعمرة بعد أفعال الأولى قبل الحلق لأنه جمع بينهما، وقد تقدم أنه مكروه في العمرتين دون الحجتين فلذا فرق في المختصر بين الحج والعمرة فأوجب في العمرة دماً للجمع بين العمرتين ولم يوجبه في الحج لأنه لو أوجبه لأوجب دمين فيما إذا أحرم بالثاني قبل الحلق للأول دم لما ذكرناه سبقاً ودم للجمع، وبه قال بعض المشايخ اتباعاً لرواية الأصل، وما في المختصر اتباع للجامع الصغير فإنه أوجب دماً واحداً للحج ، وقد علمت فيما سبق عن المحيط أن الفرق بينهما ظاهر الرواية، وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه لا يتم لأن كونه يتمكن من أداء العمرة الثانية لا يوجب الجمع فعلاً فاستويا، فالأوجه أنه ليس فيه إلا رواية الوجوب اهـ.
The chapter of Hajj, section on adding ihram to ihram. Al-Inayah: And blood sacrifice is only necessary when one enters ihram after postponing an umrah after the acts of the first before shaving, because he combined them. It has preceded that it is disliked (makruh) in two umrahs but not in two hajjs, therefore the Mukhtasar differentiated between hajj and umrah, making a dam obligatory in umrah for combining two umrahs, and not obligating it in hajj because if he obligated it, he would obligate two dams when he enters the second before shaving for the first: one dam for what we mentioned earlier and a dam for combining. Some mashayikh followed the original narration, and what is in al-Mukhtasar follows al-Jami' al-Saghir which obligated one dam for hajj. You have learned from al-Muhit that the difference between them is the apparent narration. Al-Fath al-Qadir refuted this saying it is incomplete because being able to perform the second umrah does not necessitate actual combination, so they are equal. The most correct view is that there is only the narration of obligation (wujub). End.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq discusses the ruling on combining two ihrams. The author first states the ruling that a dam (blood sacrifice) is required when one performs a second umrah after the first umrah's actions but before shaving because this constitutes combining (jama'). He then explains the basis: combining two umrahs is makruh (disliked) while combining two hajjs is not. Therefore, the Mukhtasar (by al-Quduri) differentiates, requiring dam for the former but not for the latter. The author then notes a disagreement among Hanafi scholars: some follow the 'original narration' (riwayat al-asl) which would require two dams for hajj, but the Mukhtasar follows al-Jami' al-Saghir which requires only one dam. The author reports that al-Muhit states the difference is 'apparent narration' (zahir al-riwaya), but al-Fath al-Qadir criticizes this reasoning, arguing that the ability to perform the second umrah does not constitute actual combination. The preferred view according to al-Bahr al-Raiq is that there is only one narration, which is the one that obligates dam (for combining two umrahs only). This is an intra-Hanafi dispute about which narration is authoritative.

Key Terms
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice required as compensation for certain violations during ihram.
إضافة الإحرام (idafat al-ihram): The act of entering into a second ihram while still in the state of ihram for a previous pilgrimage or umrah.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked act that does not invalidate the worship but is discouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in this passage, what is the ruling on combining two Umrahs compared to combining two Hajjs?
A) Both require a dam.
B) Neither requires a dam.
C) Combining two Umrahs requires a dam, combining two Hajjs does not.
D) Combining two Hajjs requires a dam, combining two Umrahs does not.

Key Takeaway
Combining two Umrahs before halq requires a dam because it is makruh, but combining two Hajjs does not, as per the authoritative Hanafi narration.

Combining Two Iḥrāms: Valid but with Additional Dams
Rulings on combining iḥrāms with intra-Ḥanafī disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rulings on combining two iḥrāms, identify when a dam is required, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding iḥṣār.

Core Idea
Combining two iḥrāms is valid but triggers extra dam obligations; intra-Hanafi dispute over how many animals to send at iḥṣār.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq clarifies the fiqh of adding a second iḥrām to the first—whether two ʿUmrahs or Hajj and ʿUmrah. The key principle: iḥrāms themselves do not contradict; only their performances do. The text then walks through scenarios of combination, abandonment, and prevention, revealing a three-way ikhtilāf among the Hanafi imams on the consequences of iḥṣār. Understanding these nuances will sharpen your ability to derive rulings from the school's foundational texts.

Guided Path
1
State the General Ruling
Start by identifying the baseline: combining two iḥrāms is permissible (mubāḥ). The second iḥrām becomes binding, and no dam is required for the mere act of combining; however, a dam becomes due if the first ʿUmrah was incomplete (taqṣīr left undone).
This sets the stage for the ensuing disputes.
2
Identify the Intra-Hanafī Dispute on Iḥṣār
The core ikhtilāf arises when a person with two iḥrāms (e.g., Hajj and ʿUmrah) is prevented (iḥṣār) before reaching Makkah. Abu Hanīfa requires two animals, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad each require only one, but for different reasons.
Focus on the reasoning, not just the numbers.
3
Trace Each Imām's Reasoning
Abu Hanīfa: both iḥrāms are valid and independent, so each needs its own dam. Abu Yusuf: one iḥrām (the ʿUmrah) is effectively abandoned when actions of Hajj begin, so only one dam. Muhammad: only one iḥrām (the Hajj) was binding from the start, so one dam suffices.
This reveals different views on the status of the second iḥrām.
4
Apply to Violations and Abandonment
If a violation (e.g., hunting) occurs before commencing actions, two compensations are due. If one iḥrām is abandoned, a dam for abandonment is due, and the other proceeds. The thamarah al-khilāf (practical difference) is the number of animals and the required make-up acts.
The text provides multiple sub-scenarios; focus on the principle.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilāf
The practical outcome: according to Abu Hanīfa, the prevented pilgrim sends two animals and later must make up both Hajj and ʿUmrah; according to the Ṣāḥibayn, only one animal is sent, but the number of make-up duties differs (Abu Yusuf: one Hajj and one ʿUmrah; Muhammad: only one Hajj).
This step solidifies why the ikhtilāf matters in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام لزمه الآخر ولا دم والإلزام وعليه دم قصر أو لا ومن فرغ من عمرته إلا التقصير فأحرم بأخرى لزمه دم ومن أحرم بحج ثم بعمرة ثم وقف بعرفات فقد رفض عمرته المبسوط على أنه ظاهر الرواية لأنه لا تنافي بين الإحرامين وإنما التنافي بين الأداءين. وثمرة الاختلاف فيما إذا جنى قبل الشروع فعليه دمان للجناية على إحرامين، ولو قتل صيداً لزمه قيمتان عند أبي يوسف لارتفاض إحداهما ،قبلها وإذا رفض إحداهما لزمه دم للرفض ويمضي في الأخرى ويقضي حجة وعمرة لأجل التي رفضها. وإذا أحصر قبل أن يصير إلى مكة بعث بهديين عند الإمام، وبواحد عندهما ، أما عند أبي يوسف فلأنه صار رافضاً لإحداهما، وأما عند محمد فلأنه لم يلزمه إلا أحدهما ، فإذا لم يحج في تلك السنة لزمه عمرتان وحجتان لأنه فاته حجتان في هذه السنة . وقيد بكون إحرام العمرة الثانية بعد الفراغ من العمرة الأولى إلا التقصير لأنه لو كان بعد التقصير فلا شيء عليه، وإن كانا معاً أو على التعاقب فالحكم كما تقدم في الحجتين من لزومهما عندهما خلافاً لمحمد، ومن ارتفاع أحدهما بالشروع في عمل الأخرى عند الإمام خلافاً لأبي يوسف ووجوب القضاء ودم للرفض وإن كان قبل الفراغ بعد ما طاف للأولى شوطاً رفض الثانية وعليه دم الرفض والقضاء، وكذا لو طاف الكل قبل أن يسعى ؛ فإن كان فرغ إلا الحلق لم يرفض شيئاً وعليه دم الجمع وهي مسألة المختصر، فإن حلق للأولى لزمه دم آخر للجناية على الثانية، ولو كان جامع في الأول قبل أن يطوف فأفسدها ثم أدخل الثانية يرفضها ويمضي في يتمها لأن الفاسد معتبر بالصحيح في وجوب الإتمام . وإن نوى رفض الأولى والعمل في الثانية لم يكن عليه إلا الأولى، ومن أحرم لا ينوي شيئاً فطاف ثلاثة فأقل ثم أهل بعمرة رفضها لأن الأولى تعينت عمرة حين أخذ في الطواف فحين أهل بعمرة أخرى صار جامعاً بين عمرتين الأولى حتى ! فلهذا يرفض الثانية .
Book of Hajj, Chapter on Adding Iḥrām to Iḥrām: It becomes binding upon him the other and no blood sacrifice, and the obligation and upon him a blood sacrifice whether short or not. Who completed his ʿUmrah except the taqsir and then entered into another ʿUmrah, upon him a blood sacrifice. Who entered iḥrām for Hajj then for ʿUmrah and then stood at ʿArafāt, he has abandoned his ʿUmrah. It is stated in al-Mabsūṭ as Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah because there is no contradiction between the two iḥrāms; rather the contradiction is between the performances. The fruit of the difference is when he commits a violation before commencement: upon him two blood sacrifices for violation on two iḥrāms. And if he kills game, two compensations are due according to Abū Yūsuf because one of them lapses. Before that, if he abandons one of them, a blood sacrifice is due for abandonment, and he proceeds in the other and makes up a Hajj and an ʿUmrah for the one he abandoned. If he is prevented before reaching Makkah, he sends two animals according to the Imām, and one according to the two companions. As for Abū Yūsuf, because he has become abandoner of one of them; as for Muḥammad, because only one of them became obligatory upon him. If he does not perform Hajj that year, two ʿUmrahs and two Hajjs become due because two Hajjs are missed in this year. It is conditioned that the iḥrām of the second ʿUmrah is after completion of the first ʿUmrah except the taqsir, because if it is after taqsir, nothing is upon him. If they are together or consecutively, the ruling is as stated before in the two Hajjs: that both are binding according to the two companions, contrary to Muḥammad; and that one of them is raised by commencement of the action of the other according to the Imām, contrary to Abū Yūsuf; and obligation of making up and a blood sacrifice for abandonment. If it is before completion after he has performed one circuit (tawaf) for the first, he abandons the second, and upon him blood sacrifice for abandonment and making up. Similarly if he performed all the circuits before saʿy. If he has completed except the shaving, he does not abandon anything and upon him blood sacrifice for combining. This is the issue of al-Mukhtasar. If he shaved for the first, another blood sacrifice is due for violation on the second. If he was combining in the first before tawaf and then spoiled it, then he enters the second, he abandons it and proceeds in completing it because the spoiled one is considered like the valid in obligation of completion. If he intended to abandon the first and act in the second, only the first is upon him. Who entered iḥrām without intending anything and performed three circuits or less and then pronounced talbiyah for ʿUmrah, he abandons it because the first became determined as ʿUmrah when he commenced tawaf; so when he pronounced talbiyah for another ʿUmrah, he became combining between two ʿUmrahs; thus he abandons the second.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents the general rulings on combining two iḥrāms (either two ʿUmrahs or a Hajj and an ʿUmrah). The key principle is that combining iḥrāms is valid in itself; there is no mutual exclusion between the two iḥrāms, only between their performances. The chapter begins by stating that if someone completes a ʿUmrah except for the taqsir (shortening hair) and then enters a second ʿUmrah, a dam (blood sacrifice) is required for the combination. Similarly, if one enters iḥrām for Hajj and then for ʿUmrah and then stands at ʿArafāt, the ʿUmrah is considered abandoned. The commentator notes that this is the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah position as found in al-Mabsūṭ. The 'fruit of the difference' refers to a dispute among the Ḥanafī imams regarding violations committed before commencing actions: if one commits a violation (e.g., hunting) while having two iḥrāms, two compensations are due. Abū Yūsuf holds that if one kills game, two values are owed because one iḥrām lapses. More significantly, there is a three-way dispute on what happens if one is prevented (iḥṣār) before reaching Makkah. Imam Abū Ḥanīfa says two animals must be sent (one for each iḥrām), while Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad say one animal suffices, albeit for different reasons: Abū Yūsuf considers one iḥrām abandoned, Muḥammad holds only one iḥrām was obligatory. The text then details scenarios of combining two ʿUmrahs and two Hajjs, including the conditions for when abandoning one iḥrām is required and when dam is due. The ruling emphasizes that the act of combining is permissible but brings additional obligations.

Key Terms
إحرام (iḥrām): The state of consecration for pilgrimage (Hajj or ʿUmrah), entered by intention and talbiyah.
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) required as compensation for violations or for combining iḥrāms.
ادا (adā'): Performance of the acts of Hajj or ʿUmrah individually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone completes ʿUmrah except the taqsir and then enters another ʿUmrah?
A) The second ʿUmrah is invalid and must be abandoned.
B) A dam is required for the combination, and both ʿUmrahs are valid.
C) The first ʿUmrah is automatically cancelled.
D) No blood sacrifice is required because taqsir is not an integral.

Key Takeaway
Combining two iḥrāms is valid but triggers additional wajibat; the intra-Hanafi dispute on iḥṣār shows how differing views on iḥrām validity affect the number of required sacrifices.

Distinguishing Standing from Proceeding at ʿArafāt: The Ruling on Abandoning ʿUmrah
Commentary on the ruling that standing at ʿArafāt voids a preceding ʿUmrah iḥrām

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing at ʿArafāt after entering ʿUmrah iḥrām and distinguish it from mere proceeding.

Core Idea
Standing at ʿArafāt voids a preceding ʿUmrah, but merely proceeding does not.

A common confusion in Hajj and ʿUmrah sequences is what happens when someone combines both and then reaches ʿArafāt. This lesson clarifies the precise rule: only actual standing (wufūf) at ʿArafāt causes the ʿUmrah to be abandoned, while mere proceeding (tawajjuh) does not. We also explore the proof from the hadith of ʿĀ’ishah and a subtle distinction concerning fawāt vs iḥṣār.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is standing at ʿArafāt after having entered iḥrām for ʿUmrah following iḥrām for Hajj. The ruling: the ʿUmrah becomes void and must be abandoned.
2
Distinguish wufūf from tawajjuh
The matn explicitly says 'then stood at ʿArafāt' not 'proceeded to it'. The commentator explains that mere proceeding makes one a qārin, not an abandoner.
3
Examine the dalīl
The proof is the hadith of ʿĀ’ishah where the Prophet told her to abandon her ʿUmrah (irfaḍī). This shows permissibility of abandoning an ʿUmrah.
The imperative 'irfaḍī' is taken as indicating permission (ibāḥa) in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the nuance: fawāt vs iḥṣār
The commentary adds that if Hajj is missed due to fawāt (the day of ʿArafāt passed), then one ʿUmrah is due in qadā; if due to iḥṣār (enemy/illness), then two ʿUmrahs are due because one exits both iḥrāms without action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ومن أحرم يحج ثم بعمرة ثم وقف بعرفات فقد رفض عمرته وإن توجه إليها لا) أي لا يصير رافضاً لأنه . يصير قارناً بالجمع بين الحج والعمرة لأنه مشروع في حق الآفاقي والكلام فيه لكنه مسيء بتقديم إحرام الحج على إحرام العمرة كما قدمناه في بابه، وقد تعذر عليه أداء العمرة بالوقوف إذ هي مبنية على الحج غير مشروعة، وقد تقدم الفرق بين الوقوف والتوجه. وإنما قلنا إن العمرة تحتمل الرفض لما روي عن عائشة قالت : خرجنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أن قال لها النبي : وأمشطي رأسك وارفضي عمرتك. والمراد بقوله «ثم ثم قال : وقال المصنف هكذا أطلقوه وليس بمطلق بل إن كان عدم حجه من عامه لفوات فعليه عمرة واحدة في القضاء لأجل الذي رفضه وليس عليه للفائت عمرة لأنه قد تحلل بأفعال العمرة وإن كان عدم الحج لإحصاره فعليه عمرتان في القضاء لخروجه من الإحرامين بلا فعل ا هـ. وهو تحقيق حسن كما لا يخفى ا هـ . قوله : (كما اختاره شمس (الأئمة وكذا قاضيخان والإمام المحبوبي كما في الشرنبلالية قوله :
His statement: 'Whoever enters iḥrām for Hajj then for ʿUmrah then stands at ʿArafāt, he has abandoned his ʿUmrah, and if he proceeds towards it, not). Meaning: he does not become an abandoner because he becomes a qārin (combining) between Hajj and ʿUmrah, since that is legislated for the non-Makkans. The discussion is about him, but he is blameworthy for presenting the iḥrām of Hajj before the iḥrām of ʿUmrah, as we have mentioned in its chapter. The performance of ʿUmrah becomes impossible for him by standing, since it is built upon Hajj not legislated. The difference between standing and proceeding has been mentioned earlier. We said that the ʿUmrah is capable of being abandoned due to what was narrated from ʿĀ’ishah: 'We went out with the Messenger of Allah  to the extent that the Prophet  said to her: comb your head and abandon your ʿUmrah.' The intended meaning of his statement 'then' then he said: The author said 'they have said it in an absolute manner, but it is not absolute. Rather, if his not performing Hajj that year is due to its missing, then one ʿUmrah is due in the recompense for the one he abandoned, and no ʿUmrah is due for the missed one because he has become freed by the acts of ʿUmrah. And if the not performing Hajj is due to iḥṣār, then two ʿUmrahs are due in the recompense because he exited from the two iḥrāms without action.' End quote. It is a good verification, as is not hidden. His statement: 'As chosen by Shams al-A’immah and also Qāḍīkhān and al-Imām al-Maḥbūbī as in al-Sharnablāliyyah, his statement:'
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the specific case of someone who enters iḥrām for Hajj first, then for ʿUmrah, and then stands at ʿArafāt. The matn states that this abandons the ʿUmrah, but adds the condition 'if he proceeds towards it (i.e., ʿArafāt) not' – meaning if he merely proceeds towards ʿArafāt without actually standing there, he does not become an abandoner. The commentator explains the distinction: if he proceeds to ʿArafāt without standing, he becomes a qārin (one who combines Hajj and ʿUmrah), which is permissible for non-Makkans, though he is blameworthy for reversing the order. However, once he actually stands at ʿArafāt, the ʿUmrah can no longer be performed because the time for it has passed (being built into Hajj). The commentary then cites the hadith of ʿĀ’ishah, where the Prophet told her to abandon her ʿUmrah by combing her hair, which demonstrates that an ʿUmrah iḥrām can be abandoned. The commentator further clarifies a nuance: if the missing of Hajj is due to the loss (fawāt) of the year, then only one makeup ʿUmrah is due (for the abandoned one), because the missed Hajj is already covered by the ʿUmrah acts. But if it is due to iḥṣār (prevention), then two makeup ʿUmrahs are due because the person exited both iḥrāms without performing any acts. This is a supported view.

Key Terms
وقوف (wufūf): Standing at ʿArafāt, the essential component of Hajj.
توجه (tawajjuh): Proceeding towards ʿArafāt without taking place at the actual site.
رفض (rafḍ): Abandonment of an iḥrām, permissible in specific circumstances and requiring dam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on this passage, what happens if someone entering iḥrām for both Hajj and ʿUmrah merely proceeds towards ʿArafāt without standing?
A) The ʿUmrah becomes void and must be abandoned.
B) He becomes a qārin (combining) and the ʿUmrah is valid, but he is blameworthy for reversing the order.
C) The ʿUmrah becomes invalid and requires a dam but not abandonment.
D) The Hajj becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Standing at ʿArafāt voids a preceding ʿUmrah iḥrām, requiring its abandonment and a makeup ʿUmrah, while merely proceeding does not void it.

Ruling on Tawāf of Arrival for Hajj Followed by ʿUmrah Iḥrām
Explains ruling on combining tawāf of arrival with ʿUmrah and types of dam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the dam when combining tawāf of arrival for Hajj with ʿUmrah, and distinguish between the dam of expiation (kaffāra) and the dam of thanks (shukr).

Core Idea
Combining tawāf of arrival (sunna) for Hajj with ʿUmrah requires a dam, whether you proceed or abandon.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq clarifies the situation of a pilgrim who performs the sunnah tawāf of arrival (qudūm) upon reaching Makkah for Hajj, then enters iḥrām for ʿUmrah and intends to perform both. It explains the validity of the combination, the obligation of a dam, and the recommendation to abandon the ʿUmrah. Understanding this ruling prevents confusion about the status of tawāf al-qudūm and the types of dam due in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing tawāf al-qudūm (sunna) for Hajj, then entering iḥrām for ʿUmrah and proceeding with both. The ruling: it is valid, but a dam is obligatory (wajib).
The dam is wajib because the sunnah order (ʿUmrah before Hajj) is violated.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is qiyas: analogy to the dam of qirān (combining two iḥrāms) and the general principle that violating a sunnah in worship requires compensation.
The dalil is zanni in both transmission and indication.
3
Distinguish between the two types of dam
The passage discusses two types: (1) dam kaffāra (expiation) if one proceeds with both, from which the pilgrim cannot eat; (2) dam shukr (thanks) if one abandons the ʿUmrah as recommended, similar to the dam of qirān. The mufta bihi is that it is a dam of expiation (kaffāra) and cannot be eaten.
There is intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the nature, but the practical ruling is that it is wajib and not eaten.
4
Examine the scenario of Day of Nahr
If one enters ʿUmrah on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or during Tashrīq, it is makrūh taḥrīman but binding. The pilgrim must abandon it (with dam and qadā) or proceed with a dam.
The karāha is due to conflict with remaining Hajj obligations.
5
Understand the effect of tawāf al-qudūm being sunnah
Since tawāf al-qudūm is not a rukn or wajib of Hajj but merely a sunnah for arriving at the Masjid al-Harām, it does not prevent building Hajj acts upon ʿUmrah acts. This is why the combination is valid without invalidating the Hajj.
Some scholars initially thought it might interfere, but the correct view is that it is like greeting the mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو طاف للحج ثم أحرم بعمرة ومضى عليهما يجب دم يعني لجمعه بينهما لأن الجمع بينهما مشروع فصح الإحرام بهما ، وأراد بهذا الطواف طواف القدوم وهو سنة فإن لم يأت بما هو ركن يمكنه أن يأتي بأفعال العمرة ثم بأفعال الحج، فلهذا لو مضى عليهما جاز ولزمه دم للجمع وهو دم كفارة وجبر حتى لا يأكل منه لأنه خالف السنة في هذا الجمع، وصححه في الهداية. وقول المصنف : وتدب رفضها أي العمرة يدل على أنه دم شكر وهو دم القرآن كما اختاره شمس الأئمة السرخسي، فإن محمداً قال في الجامع الصغير : وأحب إلي أن يرفض العمرة . فدل على أنه دم شكر فإنه لم يبين أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج لأن ما أتى به إنما هو سنة فيمكنه بناء أفعال الحج على أفعال العمرة فلا موجب للجبر واختاره في فتح القدير وقواه بأن طواف القدوم ليس من سنن نفس الحج بل هو سنة قدوم المسجد الحرام كركعتي التحية لغيره من المساجد، ولذا سقط بطواف آخر من مشروعات الوقت وأطال الكلام فيه. قيد بالطواف بأنه لو لم يطف لم يستحب رفضها فإذا رفضها يقضيها لصحة الشروع فيها وعليه دم لرفضها قوله : (وإن أهل بعمرة يوم النحر لزمته ولزمه الرفض والدم والقضاء) لصحة الشروع مع الكراهة التحريمية فلزمت للأول ولزم الترك تخلصاً من الإثم، وإن رفضها لزمه دم للتحلل منها بغير أفعالها، ووجب القضاء لأنه ثمرة اللزوم. وأراد بيوم النحر اليوم الذي تكره العمرة فيه وهو يوم النحر وأيام التشريق، وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان قبل الحلق أو بعده قبل طواف الزيارة أو بعده ، واختاره في الهداية وصححه الشارح لأنه بعد الحلق والطواف بقي عليه من واجبات الحج كالرمي وطواف الصدر وسنة المبيت، وقد كرهت العمرة في هذه الأيام أيضاً فيصير بانياً أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج بلا ريب وهو مكروه قوله : (فإن مضى عليها صح ويجب (دم) لأن الكراهة لمعنى في غيرها وهو كونه مشغولاً بأداء بقية أفعال الحج في هذه الأيام فيجب تخليص الوقت له تعظيماً وهو لا يعدم المشروعية لكن يلزمه الدم كفارة للجمع بين الإحرامين أو للجمع بين الأفعال الباقية فهو دم جبر لا يؤكل منه كالأول
His statement: 'So if he performed tawāf for Hajj, then entered iḥrām for ʿUmrah and proceeded with both, a dam is due' meaning, because of his combining between them, because combining is legislated, so the iḥrām for both is valid. He meant by this tawāf, the tawāf of arrival (qudūm), which is sunnah. If he does not bring what is a pillar, he can perform the acts of ʿUmrah then the acts of Hajj. For this reason, if he proceeded with both, it is permissible and a dam is due for the combination, and it is a dam of expiation and compensation, so he does not eat from it because he violated the sunnah in this combination. It is authenticated in al-Hidāyah. The author's statement: 'and it is recommended to abandon it' i.e., the ʿUmrah, indicates that it is a dam of thanks, which is the dam of qirān (combining), as chosen by Shams al-A’immah al-Sarakhsī. Indeed, Muḥammad said in al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr: 'What I love is that he abandons the ʿUmrah.' This indicates it is a dam of thanks because he does not superpose the acts of ʿUmrah upon the acts of Hajj, since what he has done is only sunnah; he can build the acts of Hajj upon the acts of ʿUmrah, so there is no cause for compensation. This is chosen in Fatḥ al-Qadīr and supported by stating that the tawāf of arrival is not from the sunan of Hajj itself, but the sunnah of arriving at the Sacred Mosque, like the two rakʿahs of greeting for other mosques. For this reason it is waived by another tawāf from the prescribed acts of the time. He elaborated on this. He conditioned by tawāf that if he had not performed tawāf, it would not be recommended to abandon it. So if he abandons it, he makes it up due to the validity of entering into it, and upon him is a dam for abandoning it. His statement: 'And if he declares talbiya for ʿUmrah on the Day of Nahr, it becomes binding upon him, and he must abandon it, and [pay] dam and make up.' Due to the validity of entering it with karāhah taḥrīmiyyah, so it became binding for the first, and it is necessary to leave it to escape sin. If he abandons it, he must pay a dam for dissolution without acts, and making up is obligatory because it is the consequence of binding. He meant by 'Day of Nahr' the day on which ʿUmrah is disliked: the Day of Nahr and the Days of Tashrīq. He mentioned absolutely, so it includes whether before shaving or after, before tawāf al-ziyārah or after. This is chosen in al-Hidāyah and authenticated by the commentator because after shaving and tawāf, there remain upon him wājibāt of Hajj like ramy, tawāf al-ṣadr, and sunnah of mabīt. ʿUmrah is disliked in these days as well, so he becomes a builder of the acts of ʿUmrah upon the acts of Hajj without doubt, and it is makrūh. His statement: 'If he proceeds with both (i.e., no abandonment), it is valid and a dam is due' because the dislikedness is due to an external meaning, i.e., being occupied with performing the remaining acts of Hajj in these days, so it is necessary to free time for it out of reverence, and it does not remove the validity; but the dam is due as expiation for combining the two iḥrāms or for combining the remaining acts. So it is a dam of compensation not to be eaten, like the first.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific scenario: a pilgrim who has performed the tawāf of arrival (qudūm) for Hajj (which is sunnah) and then enters iḥrām for ʿUmrah and intends to perform both. The ruling is that it is permissible, but a dam is required for combining this way because it goes against the sunnah order (ʿUmrah before Hajj). The dam is considered a dam of expiation (dam kaffārah) from which the pilgrim cannot eat. However, it is recommended (nadb) to abandon the ʿUmrah, and if he does so, the dam becomes a dam of thanks (dam shukr) like the dam of qirān, which again he cannot eat from. The commentator explains that the tawāf of arrival is not a fundamental part of Hajj but is merely a greeting for the mosque, so it does not conflict with building Hajj on ʿUmrah. The passage also addresses entering ʿUmrah on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) and the days of Tashrīq: it is makrūh taḥrīman to do so, but if one does, it is binding and must be abandoned with dam and qadā. If one proceeds with it regardless, the ʿUmrah is valid but requires a dam. The underlying reason is that during these days, the pilgrim is occupied with remaining obligatory acts of Hajj, so adding ʿUmrah causes a disliked combination. The dam serves as compensation.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (ṭawāf al-qudūm): The tawāf performed upon arrival at Makkah, considered sunnah by Hanafis.
دم الشكر (dam al-shukr): A blood sacrifice offered as gratitude for the ability to combine or for the validity of the ʿUmrah after abandonment.
كراهة تحريمية (karāha taḥrīmiyya): A level of dislike closer to prohibition; an act that is sinful but not definitively forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the dam when someone performs tawāf of arrival for Hajj, then enters ʿUmrah and proceeds with both?
A) It is a dam of thanks (shukr) that the person can eat from.
B) It is a dam of expiation (kaffāra) that cannot be eaten.
C) No dam is required because the tawāf is sunnah.
D) Only a dam of abandonment is due.

Key Takeaway
Performing tawāf of arrival (sunnah) for Hajj and then entering ʿUmrah requires a dam, whether you proceed or abandon the ʿUmrah.

Missing Hajj: Ruling on Entering a New Iḥrām
Ruling that a fā'it al-ḥajj must abandon any new iḥrām.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a person who misses Hajj and then enters a new iḥrām, and explain the reasoning based on the prohibition of combining two identical pilgrimages.

Core Idea
One who misses Hajj dissolves his iḥrām through ʿUmrah acts; any new iḥrām for ʿUmrah or Hajj must be abandoned.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hajj: a pilgrim who misses the essential standing at ʿArafāt (the fā'it al-ḥajj) and then enters a new iḥrām for ʿUmrah or Hajj. The text gives a clear ruling that this new iḥrām must be abandoned. We will unpack the reasoning and the key terms to understand why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and action
The subject is 'whoever misses Hajj' (fā'it al-ḥajj). The action is 'then enters iḥrām for ʿUmrah or Hajj'.
Note the condition: the person is already in a state of iḥrām from the missed Hajj.
2
State the ruling
The ruling: 'he abandons it' (rafḍuhā). The new iḥrām is invalid and must be cancelled.
3
Understand the reasoning
The fā'it al-ḥajj becomes free (taḥallul) by performing the acts of ʿUmrah without his iḥrām being transformed. Entering a new iḥrām for ʿUmrah would combine two ʿUmrahs; for Hajj, two Hajjs. Both combinations are invalid.
The text uses 'rafḍ' (abandonment) because the second iḥrām cannot be corrected.
4
Apply the term fā'it al-ḥajj
Missing Hajj does not waste the iḥrām; it is dissolved by performing ʿUmrah. The pilgrim must then make up the Hajj in a future year.
This distinguishes the fā'it from a normal pilgrim who may combine ʿUmrah and Hajj as a qārin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن فاته الحج فأحرم بعمرة أو حجة رفضها لأن فائت الحج يتحلل بأفعال العمرة من غير أن ينقلب إحرامه (فيصير جامعاً بينا العمرتين (الخ) راجع إلى قوله وأحرم بعمرة . وقوله «أو جامعاً بين حجتين» راجع إلى قوله «أو حجة».)
His statement: 'Whoever misses Hajj and then enters iḥrām for an ʿUmrah or a Hajj, he abandons it, because the one who missed Hajj becomes free (from iḥrām) by the acts of ʿUmrah without his iḥrām being transformed (so he becomes combining between two ʿUmrahs) – this refers back to his statement 'and he enters iḥrām for ʿUmrah'. And his statement 'or combining between two Hajjs' refers back to his statement 'or a Hajj'.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This short passage provides the ruling for a person who missed Hajj (i.e., the standing at ʿArafāt was missed) and then enters a new iḥrām for either ʿUmrah or Hajj. The ruling is that the new iḥrām must be abandoned (rafḍ). The reason is that the original iḥrām for the missed Hajj is dissolved by performing the acts of ʿUmrah (i.e., the person emerges from iḥrām by doing tawāf, saʿy, and shaving). If he then enters a new iḥrām for ʿUmrah, he would effectively be combining two ʿUmrahs, which is the same issue as earlier. Similarly, if he enters for Hajj, he would be combining two Hajjs. In either case, the second iḥrām is invalid and must be abandoned. The final notes clarify the textual references.

Key Terms
فائت الحج (fā'it al-ḥajj): One who missed the essential standing at ʿArafāt and thus his Hajj is invalid; he must perform ʿUmrah and make up Hajj.
تحلل (taḥallul): Exiting the state of iḥrām by performing certain actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what should a person who missed Hajj and then entered iḥrām for ʿUmrah do?
A) Proceed with both as a qārin.
B) Complete the ʿUmrah and the missed Hajj in one set of actions.
C) Abandon the ʿUmrah iḥrām because it would cause combining two ʿUmrahs.
D) Abandon the original missed Hajj iḥrām and continue with the new ʿUmrah.

Key Takeaway
A person who misses Hajj must not enter a new iḥrām for either ʿUmrah or Hajj; such a second iḥrām is invalid and must be abandoned.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Adding Ihram to Ihram: Combining Hajj and Umrah
Ruling with proof: adding umrah to hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pilgrim performs tawaf al-qudum for hajj then enters ihram for umrah, and identify when a dam is required and whether rejection of the later ihram is recommended.

Core Idea
Adding umrah to hajj after tawaf al-qudum is valid but requires a dam; rejection of the later ihram is recommended to avoid it.

In this lesson, we will examine a case from the Hanafi school: a pilgrim who has already performed tawaf al-qudum (the sunnah tawaf upon arriving in Makkah) for hajj then decides to enter ihram for umrah and proceed with both. What is the ruling? Is it valid? Does it require a dam? Should he reject the umrah? The source text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies these points and also discusses the situation when umrah is entered on the Day of Nahr. By the end, you will be able to apply these rulings and understand when a dam is of gratitude (shukr) versus compensation (jabr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The pilgrim performs tawaf al-qudum (sunnah) for hajj, then enters ihram for umrah and proceeds with both. The ruling is that the combination is valid but a dam is obligatory.
The tawaf performed is not a pillar but a sunnah, so the umrah can be added without invalidating hajj.
2
Determine the type of dam
There is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf: the dam is either of expiation (jabr) or gratitude (shukr). The preferred view (mukhtar) is that it is a dam of gratitude, as chosen by al-Sarakhsi and in Fath al-Qadir.
If it were a dam of expiation, the pilgrim could not eat from it; if of gratitude, he may eat from it.
3
Understand the recommendation to reject the umrah
Rejection (rafd) of the umrah is recommended (mandub) to avoid the dam altogether. If the pilgrim rejects, he must still perform the umrah later as make-up (qada) and pay a dam for the rejection.
Rejection is only recommended when tawaf al-qudum has been performed; otherwise, it is not recommended.
4
Apply to the case of ihram on the Day of Nahr
If a pilgrim enters ihram for umrah on the Day of Nahr or the Days of Tashriq, it is disliked (makruh tahrimi) but valid. He must reject it, pay a dam, and make up the umrah. If he continues, it is valid but a dam is required as expiation.
The dislike is due to being occupied with the remaining obligations of hajj on those days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام وإن توجه إليها لا فلو طاف للحج ثم أحرم بعمرة ومضى عليهما يجب دم وندب رفضها وإن أهل بعمرة يوم النحر لزمته ولزمه الرفض والدم والقضاء فإن مضى عليها صح ويجب دم ومن فاته الحج فأحرم بعمرة أو حجة رفضها والله أعلم.
بعمره
رة أنه أحرم بالعمرة ولم يأت بأكثر أشواطها حتى وقف بعرفات فالإتيان بالأقل كالعدم قوله : (فلو طاف للحج ثم أحرم بعمرة ومضى عليهما يجب دم يعني لجمعه بينهما لأن الجمع بينهما مشروع فصح الإحرام بهما ، وأراد بهذا الطواف طواف القدوم وهو سنة فإن لم يأت بما هو ركن يمكنه أن يأتي بأفعال العمرة ثم بأفعال الحج، فلهذا لو مضى عليهما جاز ولزمه دم للجمع وهو دم كفارة وجبر حتى لا يأكل منه لأنه خالف السنة في هذا الجمع، وصححه في الهداية. وقول المصنف : وندب رفضها أي العمرة يدل على أنه دم شكر وهو دم القرآن كما اختاره شمس الأئمة السرخسي، فإن محمداً قال في الجامع الصغير : وأحب إلي أن يرفض العمرة . فدل على أنه دم شكر فإنه لم يبين أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج لأن ما أتى به إنما هو سنة فيمكنه بناء أفعال الحج على أفعال العمرة فلا موجب للجبر واختاره في فتح القدير وقواه بأن طواف القدوم ليس من سنن نفس الحج بل هو سنة قدوم المسجد الحرام كركعتي التحية لغيره من المساجد، ولذا سقط بطواف آخر من مشروعات الوقت وأطال الكلام فيه. قيد بالطواف بأنه لو لم يطف لم يستحب رفضها فإذا رفضها يقضيها لصحة الشروع فيها وعليه دم لرفضها قوله : (وإن أهل بعمرة يوم النحر لزمته ولزمه الرفض والدم والقضاء) لصحة الشروع مع الكراهة التحريمية فلزمت للأول ولزم الترك تخلصاً من الإثم، وإن رفضها لزمه دم للتحلل منها بغير أفعالها، ووجب القضاء لأنه ثمرة اللزوم. وأراد بيوم النحر اليوم الذي تكره العمرة فيه وهو يوم النحر وأيام التشريق، وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان قبل الحلق أو بعده قبل طواف الزيارة أو بعده ، واختاره في الهداية وصححه الشارح لأنه بعد الحلق والطواف بقي عليه من واجبات الحج كالرمي وطواف الصدر وسنة المبيت، وقد كرهت العمرة في هذه الأيام أيضاً فيصير بانياً أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج بلا ريب وهو مكروه قوله : (فإن مضى عليها صح ويجب (دم) لأن الكراهة لمعنى في غيرها وهو كونه مشغولاً بأداء بقية أفعال الحج في هذه الأيام فيجب تخليص الوقت له تعظيماً وهو لا يعدم المشروعية لكن يلزمه الدم كفارة للجمع بين الإحرامين أو للجمع بين الأفعال الباقية فهو دم جبر لا يؤكل منه كالأول قوله : (ومن فاته الحج فأحرم بعمرة أو حجة رفضها لأن فائت الحج يتحلل بأفعال العمرة من غير أن ينقلب إحرامه
(فيصير جامعاً بينا العمرتين (الخ) راجع إلى قوله وأحرم بعمرة . وقوله «أو جامعاً بين حجتين» راجع إلى قوله «أو حجة».
Book of Hajj: Chapter on Adding Ihram to Ihram. If he heads to her? No. So if he performed tawaf for hajj then entered ihram for umrah and continued with both, a dam is obligatory and it is recommended to reject it. And if he entered ihram for umrah on the Day of Nahr, it becomes binding upon him and he must reject it, pay a dam, and make up. And if he continued with both, it is valid and a dam is obligatory. And whoever misses hajj and then enters ihram for umrah or hajj, he must reject it. And Allah knows best. With umrah? He that he entered ihram for umrah and did not perform most of its circuits until he stood at Arafat, so performing the lesser is like non-performance. His saying: (So if he performed tawaf for hajj then entered ihram for umrah and continued with both, a dam is obligatory) means due to combining them, because combining them is legislated, so ihram for both is valid. He meant by this tawaf the tawaf of arrival, which is sunnah. If he did not perform what is a pillar, he can perform the actions of umrah then the actions of hajj. For this reason, if he continued with both, it is permissible and a dam is required for combining, and it is a dam of expiation and compensation such that he does not eat from it, because he violated the sunnah in this combination. And he corrected it in al-Hidayah. The author's saying: 'and it is recommended to reject it' i.e. the umrah, indicates that it is a dam of gratitude, which is the dam of qiran, as chosen by Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi, for Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'I prefer that he reject the umrah.' So it indicates that it is a dam of gratitude, for he did not superimpose the actions of umrah upon the actions of hajj because what he performed is only sunnah, so he can build the actions of hajj upon the actions of umrah, thus there is no cause for compensation. And he chose this in Fath al-Qadir and strengthened it by saying that the tawaf of arrival is not from the sunnah of hajj itself, but rather it is a sunnah of arriving at the Sacred Mosque, like the two rak'ahs of greeting for other mosques, and therefore it is dropped by another tawaf from the prescribed deeds of the time, and he spoke at length. He restricted it to tawaf: if he did not perform tawaf, rejection is not recommended. So if he rejects it, he makes it up due to the validity of having started it, and he incurs a dam for rejecting it. His saying: (And if he entered ihram for umrah on the Day of Nahr, it becomes binding upon him and he must reject it, pay a dam, and make up) due to the validity of starting it with tahrimi dislike, so it becomes binding on him for the first, and leaving it is obligatory to escape sin. And if he rejects it, he incurs a dam for leaving it without performing its actions, and make-up is obligatory because it is the fruit of binding. He meant by 'Day of Nahr' the day on which umrah is disliked, i.e. the Day of Nahr and the Days of Tashriq. He made it general, including whether before or after shaving, before or after tawaf al-ziyarah. He chose this in al-Hidayah and the commentator corrected it, because after shaving and tawaf, there remain upon him obligations of hajj like stoning and farewell tawaf and the sunnah of staying overnight, and umrah is disliked on these days as well, so he becomes one who builds the actions of umrah upon the actions of hajj without doubt, and it is makruh. His saying: (If he continued with both, it is valid and a dam is required) because the dislike is for an external reason, i.e. his being occupied with performing the remaining actions of hajj on these days, so it is necessary to free time for it out of reverence, yet it is not devoid of legitimacy, but the dam is due as expiation for combining the two ihrams or for combining the remaining actions. So it is a dam of compensation, not eaten from, like the first. His saying: (And whoever misses hajj and then enters ihram for umrah or hajj, he must reject it) because the one who missed hajj becomes free by the actions of umrah without his ihram changing? (So he becomes combining between two umrahs (etc.) refers to his saying 'and entered ihram for umrah'. And his saying 'or combining between two hajjs' refers to his saying 'or hajj'.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the chapter 'Adding Ihram to Ihram' from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses cases where a pilgrim, after starting hajj, performs actions related to umrah or vice versa. The author first states that if a person performs tawaf for hajj (specifically the tawaf of arrival, which is sunnah) and then enters ihram for umrah, and proceeds with both, a dam is required due to combining two ihrams in a legally disapproved manner. However, rejection of the umrah is recommended to avoid the dam. The dam in this case is a 'dam of gratitude' (shukr) according to Imam Muhammad and al-Sarakhsi, meaning it is not a penalty but a voluntary offering, since the tawaf performed is not part of the hajj itself. If the pilgrim does not perform any tawaf before adding umrah, rejection is not recommended. Next, the text discusses entering ihram for umrah on the Day of Nahr and the Days of Tashriq. This is disliked (tahriman) because one is engaged in the remaining obligations of hajj. Nevertheless, the ihram is valid and binding; to escape sin, one must reject the umrah, pay a dam, and perform the umrah later. If one continues with both, the combination is valid but a dam is required as expiation (jabr). Finally, if a person misses hajj and then enters ihram for umrah or another hajj, he must reject the second ihram because he is already in the state of a missed hajj and must perform umrah instead. The rejection incurs a dam and a make-up. The commentary clarifies that the missed hajj pilgrim is like someone who is led in prayer (muqtadi) in terms of restriction but is independent in performance, so he must recite (in prayer analogy).

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) that is required as a penalty for violating the rules of ihram or as a voluntary offering.
رفض (rafd): The act of canceling or abandoning one of the two ihrams (usually the later one) to avoid combining them in a disapproved manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim performs tawaf al-qudum for hajj and then enters ihram for umrah and continues with both, what is the ruling?
A) The combination is invalid; he must cancel the umrah.
B) The combination is valid but a dam is required and rejection of the umrah is recommended.
C) The combination is valid with no penalty.
D) He must abandon the hajj and perform umrah only.

Key Takeaway
Adding umrah to hajj after tawaf al-qudum is valid but requires a dam; rejection of the later ihram is recommended to avoid it.

Ihsaar: Definition and Ruling for the Prevented Pilgrim
Defines ihsaar and states the ruling to send a sacrificial animal to become free from ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ihsaar, identify its causes, and apply the ruling that a muhsar sends a sacrificial animal (hady) to become free from ihram.

Core Idea
Ihsaar: a pilgrim prevented by any obstacle may send a sacrificial animal to release ihram.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the chapter on Ihsaar, a rare contingency that affects a pilgrim's ability to complete Hajj or Umrah. The author defines the term, clarifies its linguistic and legal scope, and provides the Quranic basis for the ruling: a prevented pilgrim may send a sacrificial animal to become free from ihram. Understanding this ruling is essential for recognizing when the obligation to complete the pilgrimage is suspended and what remedy is prescribed.

Guided Path
1
Define ihsaar linguistically and legally
Identify the linguistic distinction between ihsaar (prevention by illness) and hasr (by enemy) and the majority view that ihsaar covers both. In shari'ah, it is prevention from standing at Arafat and tawaf.
The verse (2:196) uses 'ahsartum' which the majority interprets broadly.
2
Identify causes that constitute ihsaar
List the causes mentioned: enemy, illness, loss of provisions, death of mahram, etc. Note the condition of inability to proceed even with hardship.
If one can walk despite loss of provisions, he is not muhsar.
3
State the ruling: sending a hady
The muhsar may send a sheep to be slaughtered at the Haram and then become free. For a qarin, two animals. This is a wajib for release.
The use of 'li' indicates permissibility of waiting; sacrifice is only for necessity.
4
Note the optional waiting period
The pilgrim may wait until the obstacle is removed; if he catches Hajj, he proceeds; otherwise, he performs umrah to become free.
This distinguishes ihsaar from fawat (missing Hajj entirely).
5
Distinguish muhsar from one who misses Hajj (fawat)
In fawat, the pilgrim misses the standing at Arafat and must complete umrah and make up; in ihsaar, the obstacle occurs before completion and a hady suffices.
Ihsaar is a rare contingency; fawat is another.

Chapter of Ihsaar. For one who is prevented by enemy or illness, he may send a sheep to be slaughtered on his behalf and then become free. And if he was a qarin, he sends two dams. The ihram of umrah makes him combining two umrahs in terms of actions, so rejection becomes necessary for him, as if he had entered ihram for both, or combining two hajjs in terms of ihram, so he must reject the second, as if he had entered ihram for two hajjs, and make-up is necessary due to the validity of starting, and a dam for rejection by becoming free before its time. And they differed in its linguistic meaning: It was said that ihsaar is for illness and hasr for enemy. According to this, His saying 'then if you are prevented' is to state the ruling for illness, and it is annexed to prevention by enemy by primary indication, because prevention by enemy is tangible and one cannot proceed, unlike illness where it is possible by camel litter or vehicle. The majority hold that ihsaar is prevention, whether from fear, illness, inability, or enemy, and this was chosen in al-Kashshaf. In al-Mughrib: hasr is prevention from the measure of talab; it is said 'ahsara al-hajj' if fear or illness prevents him from reaching to complete his hajj or umrah, and if a ruler or overpowering preventer prevents him in prison or city, it is said 'husira'. This is the well-known. In shari'ah, it is prevention of standing (at Arafat) and tawaf. Then if he catches the hajj, fine; otherwise, he becomes free by umrah. Thus becoming free by sacrificing a hady is only for necessity so that his ihram does not become prolonged and difficult for him, as the commentator mentioned. So what occurs in al-Mabsut with 'ala is out of place. And he indicated by mentioning enemy and illness every prevention, so he is considered muhsar by loss of provisions, death of the woman's mahram or her husband on the road. And he stipulated in al-Tajnis inability to walk in case of loss of provisions; if he is able to walk, he is not muhsar. He explained in al-Mabsut that it is not far that walking is not required initially but becomes required after starting, just as a voluntary hajj is not required initially but completion becomes required once started. . . Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq begins a new chapter on Ihsaar, meaning prevention that prevents a pilgrim from completing hajj or umrah. The author first provides the ruling: a person prevented by enemy or illness may send a sheep (or goat) to be slaughtered at the Haram on his behalf, and then he becomes free from ihram. If the person was performing qiran (combining hajj and umrah), he must send two animals. The text then digresses into the case of someone who misses hajj (fawat) and enters ihram for umrah, which is similar to the earlier section; but this is likely a repetition or a note from the commentary. The core of the chapter is the definition of ihsaar: linguistically, some distinguish between ihsaar (prevention by illness) and hasr (by enemy), but the majority consider both as prevention. In Islamic law, ihsaar is defined as prevention from standing at Arafat (in hajj) or from tawaf. The prophet (peace be upon him) experienced ihsaar (by enemy) but not fawat, so ihsaar is given priority. The ruling is based on the Quranic verse (2:196): 'then if you are prevented, then whatever is easy from the sacrificial animal.' The use of the preposition 'li' (for) indicates that it is permissible for the muhsar to wait until the obstacle is removed, and if he catches the hajj, he proceeds; otherwise, he becomes free by umrah. The sacrifice is only for necessity to avoid prolonged ihram. The conditions for being muhsar include inability to walk in case of loss of provisions; if one is able, he is not muhsar. The definition of ihsaar in shari'ah is prevention from standing at Arafat and tawaf; for umrah, it includes prevention from tawaf and sa'i (although sa'i is not a rukn in umrah according to the Hanafi school).

Key Terms
إحصار (ihsaar): Legal prevention from completing hajj or umrah due to an obstacle such as enemy, illness, or inability, requiring a sacrifice to become free from ihram.
هدي (hady): An animal (sheep, goat, cow, or camel) sent to the Haram for sacrifice as part of the rites or as a penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'فإن أحصرتم فما استيسر من الهدى' indicate regarding the muhsar?
A) He must continue the pilgrimage even if unable, and the sacrifice is optional.
B) He may send a sacrificial animal to become free from ihram, or wait and complete later if possible.
C) He becomes free automatically without any action.
D) He must perform qada (make-up) and offer a sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
Ihsaar in the Hanafi school includes any prevention from completing Hajj or Umrah, and the remedy is to send a sacrificial animal to become free from ihram.

Definition and Basic Ruling of Ihsaar
Defines ihsaar and gives ruling for muhsar with proof and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ihsaar linguistically and legally, and state the ruling and conditions for a muhsar in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A prevented muhrim may send a sacrifice and become halal – necessity overcomes hardship.

This passage introduces the chapter on ihsaar, a rare occurrence where a person in ihram is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah. It defines the term both linguistically and legally, and then outlines the basic ruling: the muhsar may send a sacrificial animal to be slaughtered in the Haram, thereby becoming halal. The proof is from Quran 2:196. The author also discusses conditions and variations for a qarin.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic meaning of ihsaar
The passage notes disagreement: some restrict ihsaar to illness and hasr to enemy, but the majority consider ihsaar as any prevention.
Look for the phrase 'الأكثر على أن الإحصار هو المنع'.
2
Identify the legal definition
In the Sacred Law, ihsaar is prevention from wuquf (standing at Arafat) and tawaf (circumambulation). The text notes that it also applies to Umrah.
The author adds 'or Tawaf and Sa'ee' for Umrah.
3
Extract the ruling from the verse
Quran 2:196 is cited: 'فإن أحصرتم فما استيسر من الهدى'. The Hanafi school takes the command as wajib: send a sacrificial animal.
The command (amr) implies wujub in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the ruling to different scenarios
For a normal muhrim: send one sheep. For a qarin (combining Hajj and Umrah): send two. For loss of provisions: inability to walk is a condition. For waiting: it's permissible to wait until the obstacle is removed.
The condition of inability is crucial; if able to walk, one is not muhsar.

If he is a qarin (combining Hajj and Umrah), he sends two blood (sacrifices). His statement: '(And in the Sacred Law, it is prevention from Wuquf and Tawaf)' said in al-Nahr: It does not include ihsaar from Umrah, and it will come that it is verified; so it should be increased with 'or Tawaf and Sa'ee' end quote. That is, it will come in the statement of the text 'And upon the one performing Umrah' i.e. if he is prevented from Umrah, but it will come that Sa'ee is wajib in Umrah, not rukn, so there is no need to mention it, so it has no rukn left.

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Ihsaar (prevention/obstruction) in the book of Hajj. Ihsaar is a rare occurrence where a person who has entered into ihram is prevented from completing the rituals. The basic ruling is that such a person may send a sacrificial animal (a sheep or more) to be slaughtered in the Haram, and then he becomes halal (released from ihram). If one is performing both Hajj and Umrah together (qarin), two sacrifices are required. The author discusses the linguistic meaning: some distinguish between ihsaar (for illness) and hasr (for enemy), but the majority consider ihsaar as any prevention. The legal definition is prevention from standing at Arafat (wuquf) and circumambulation (tawaf). The proof is from Quran 2:196. The commentator clarifies that the wording 'li-man' (for one who) implies that if he remains patient and returns home without becoming halal until the fear passes, it is permissible. The sacrificial slaughter is only for necessity. The condition is that one is unable to proceed; if he can walk, he is not considered muhsar. The passage also clarifies that the definition should include Umrah, and that sa'ee is wajib not rukn in Umrah.

Key Terms
الإحصار (al-ihsaar): Prevention from completing Hajj/Umrah rituals after entering ihram due to an external obstacle.
الحصر (al-hasr): Prevention specifically by an enemy or authority (according to some).
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal offered in the Haram as part of Hajj rituals or compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a prevented muhrim may send a sacrificial animal and become halal, based on Quran 2:196 and the principle of removing hardship.
